 window.IcreateElementChangeListener= function (selector, callback) {
    const initializedNodes = new Set([]);

    document.querySelectorAll(selector).forEach((node) => {
        callback(node);
        initializedNodes.add(node);
    });

    const mutationObserver = new MutationObserver(() => {
        const nodes = document.querySelectorAll(selector);
        nodes.forEach((node) => {
            if (!initializedNodes.has(node)) {
                callback(node);
                initializedNodes.add(node);
            }
        });
    });

    mutationObserver.observe(document.body, {
        childList: true,
        subtree: true,
    });
}

 window.setCookie__ = function (cname,cvalue,exdays) {
    var d = new Date();
    d.setTime(d.getTime() + (exdays * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000));
    var expires = "expires="+d.toUTCString();
   
    document.cookie = cname + "=" + cvalue + ";" + expires +";path=/"; ;
}

window.getCookie= function (cname) {
    var name = cname + "=";
    var decodedCookie = decodeURIComponent(document.cookie);
    var ca = decodedCookie.split(';');
    for(var i = 0; i < ca.length; i++) {
        var c = ca[i];
        while (c.charAt(0) == ' ') {
            c = c.substring(1);
        }
        if (c.indexOf(name) == 0) {
            return c.substring(name.length, c.length);
        }
    }
    return "";
}

width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_8_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_8_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 8}, {"amp": "\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_9_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_9_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>After being threatened with extinction, the American bald eagle population has quadrupled since 2009 — a swift recovery that Martha Williams, deputy director of the U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service, calls "one of the most remarkable conservation success stories of all time," <a href="https://apnews.com/article/bald-eagle-population-soars-united-states-70982fdda4b8f12ce7736ea5df0b9122" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">AP News reported</a>. </p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/american-bald-eagle-population" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651224833" data-published-at="1616783363" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;A &lt;a href="https://www.fws.gov/migratorybirds/pdf/management/bald-eagle-population-size-2020.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;report&lt;/a&gt; released Wednesday by The U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service estimated 316,700 individual bald eagles are living in the lower 48, including more than 71,400 nesting pairs. Scientists say the bald eagle's return highlights the importance of decades of &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/conservation"&gt;conservation&lt;/a&gt; efforts, &lt;a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/25/climate/how-many-bald-eagles-united-states.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;The New York Times reported&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"The strong return of this treasured bird reminds us of our nation's shared resilience and the importance of being responsible stewards of our lands and waters that bind us together,″ Interior Secretary Deb Haaland said at her first public appearance since being sworn in as the first Native American cabinet secretary, AP News reported.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/american-bald-eagle-population" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651224833" data-published-at="1616783363" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;p&gt;In 1963, the bald eagle numbers were at an "all-time low" of 417 known nesting pairs, according to AP News. But after actions like banning the pesticide DDT and placing the national bird on the &lt;a href="http://www.ecowatch.com/tag/endangered-species" target="_self"&gt;endangered species&lt;/a&gt; list, bald eagle populations grew.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"The bald eagle has always been considered a sacred species to American Indian people," Haaland said, according to The New York Times. "Similarly it's sacred to our nation as America's national symbol."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Over the span of 2018 and 2019, the U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service's Migratory Bird Program conducted aerial observations over popular eagle nesting areas to estimate populations, according to a &lt;a href="https://www.fws.gov/news/ShowNews.cfm?ref=america%E2%80%99s-bald-eagle-population-continues-to-soar&amp;amp;_ID=36871" target="_blank"&gt;news release&lt;/a&gt;. "The Service continues to work with our partners in state and federal agencies, tribes, non-government organizations and with private landowners to ensure that our nation's symbol continues to flourish," Williams said in the release.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/american-bald-eagle-population" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651224833" data-published-at="1616783363" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;p&gt;But the eagle's success story shouldn't distract from the ongoing threats American birds still face today. In 2019, the National Audubon Society released a &lt;a href="https://www.audubon.org/news/new-audubon-science-two-thirds-north-american-birds-risk-extinction-due-climate" target="_blank"&gt;report&lt;/a&gt; warning that two-thirds of American bird species were at risk of extinction due to climate change, &lt;a href="https://www.npr.org/2021/03/25/981272794/once-imperiled-americas-bald-eagle-populations-are-soaring" target="_blank"&gt;NPR reported&lt;/a&gt;. And a recent &lt;a href="https://science.sciencemag.org/content/366/6461/120" target="_blank"&gt;study&lt;/a&gt; by the Cornell Lab of Ornithology found over the past 50 years, American bird populations have dropped by about one-third.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Just because a species hasn't gone extinct or isn't even necessarily close to extinction, it might still be in trouble," Elise Zipkin, a quantitative ecologist at Michigan State University, &lt;a href="https://www.npr.org/2019/09/19/762090471/north-america-has-lost-3-billion-birds-scientists-say" target="_blank"&gt;told NPR&lt;/a&gt; after the Cornell studies publication. "We need to be thinking about conservation efforts for that."&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/american-bald-eagle-population" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651224833" data-published-at="1616783363" id="rebelltitem4">&lt;p&gt;The report on the bald eagle's recovery comes at the same time scientists identified a mysterious disease that has been killing bald eagles and other birds in the U.S. for more than 25 years, &lt;a href="https://www.sciencemag.org/news/2021/03/after-more-2-decades-searching-scientists-finger-cause-mass-eagle-deaths" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Science reported&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A neurological disease that paralyzes and kills bald eagles and other birds is linked to a new species of bacteria that grows on an invasive aquatic weed, the scientists &lt;a href="https://www.sciencemag.org/news/2021/03/after-more-2-decades-searching-scientists-finger-cause-mass-eagle-deaths" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;found&lt;/a&gt;. While the invasive weed is expected to spread, scientists celebrate their discovery — finally identifying an unknown killer and equipped with the knowledge to help protect birds in the future.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;News of the bald eagle's recovery has also been celebrated by conservationists and scientists who see the new interior secretary playing a larger role in helping species, threatened and listed as endangered, recover.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"We will be taking a closer look at all of those revisions and considering what steps to take to ensure that all of us — states, Indian tribes, private landowners and federal agencies — have the tools we need to conserve America's natural heritage and strengthen our economy," said Haaland, according to AP News. "We have an obligation to do so because future generations must also experience our beautiful outdoors, the way many of us have been blessed."&lt;/p&gt;</div>

<div class="post-tags-primary">

<h6 class="widget__headline h6">
<a aria-label="Atlantic Coast Sea Levels Are Rising at Fastest Rate in 2,000 Years, Study Finds" class="widget__headline-text custom-post-headline" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/atlantic-sea-level-rise-2651224578.html">
        Atlantic Coast Sea Levels Are Rising at Fastest Rate in 2,000 Years, Study Finds
    </a>
</h6>
<div class="social-author clearfix">
<div class="social-author__avatar image">
<div class="cover-all image" style='background-image: url("https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8xNzQxMzM2NS9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY2OTE1NTE2M30.aHAnjzcgPkB6_WqIedJyVdqvxXmBk3A_csOfZcTG7ek/img.jpg?width=210")'></div>
</div>
<a class="social-author__name" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/u/oliviarosane">Olivia Rosane</a>
</div>
<div class="social-date">
<span class="social-date__text">2h</span>
</div>
<a class="widget__section js-load-brick-on-click" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/oceans/">Oceans</a>
</div><div class="widget__head"><a aria-label="Atlantic Coast Sea Levels Are Rising at Fastest Rate in 2,000 Years, Study Finds" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/atlantic-sea-level-rise-2651224578.html">

"\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_8_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 8}, true, "new_amp": "\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_9_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>Yet another study has confirmed the unprecedented impacts of the <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change/" target="_self">climate crisis</a>: Sea levels along the eastern U.S. are rising at their fastest rate in 2,000 years. </p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/atlantic-sea-level-rise" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651224578" data-published-at="1616782127" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;Researchers led by a team at the University of Rutgers studied &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/sea-level-rise" target="_self"&gt;sea level rise&lt;/a&gt; at six sites along the Atlantic coast. They found that the rate of change between 1900 and 2000 was more than double the average for the period between year 0 and 1800, &lt;a href="https://www.rutgers.edu/news/sea-level-rise-20th-century-was-fastest-2000-years-along-much-east-coast" target="_blank"&gt;Rutgers Today reported&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"The increasing influence of the global component is the most significant change in the sea-level budgets at all six sites," the study authors wrote.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The research, &lt;a href="https://www.nature.com/articles/s41467-021-22079-2" target="_blank"&gt;published in Nature Communications&lt;/a&gt; on Tuesday, focused on sea level sites in Connecticut, New York City, North Jersey, South Jersey (Leeds Point and Cape May Courthouse) and North Carolina. The scientists examined sea-level budgets, which are the totality of regional, local and global factors that influence sea level change. Examples of regional factors include land subsidence, or sinking, while local factors include groundwater withdrawal, Rutgers Today explained. The study is the first to examine these factors across a large time frame at the Atlantic sites. Most sea level budget studies have only focused on the 20th and 21st centuries, and only on the global level.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The research found that the dominant force driving sea level change had shifted. During the totality of the 2,000 year period, land subsidence caused by the retreating Laurentide ice sheet drove the change.&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;However, in the last century, global forces took over.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/atlantic-sea-level-rise" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651224578" data-published-at="1616782127" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style="background-color: initial;"&gt;"Where it used to be this regional land sinking being the dominant force, now it's this global component, which is driven by the ice melt and warming of the oceans," Jennifer S. Walker, lead author and Rutgers University-New Brunswick postdoctoral associate, told &lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.cnn.com/2021/03/26/weather/sea-level-rise-accelerating-east-coast/index.html" target="_blank" style="background-color: initial;"&gt;CNN&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span style="background-color: initial;"&gt;.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Since 1950, the global climate crisis has driven 36 to 50 percent of sea level rise at all six sites, the authors determined.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The findings aren't only important for understanding the scale of the current crisis, but also for helping policymakers deal with its consequences. Rising sea levels can increase sunny-day &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/flooding" target="_self"&gt;floods&lt;/a&gt; and make storms such as 2012's &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/hurricane-sandy" target="_self"&gt;Hurricane Sandy&lt;/a&gt; more extreme.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"The impacts from a big storm like that are just going to be exacerbated on top of (the rising seas)," Walker told CNN.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;That is why the study chose to study individual locations across a wide period.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Having a thorough understanding of sea-level change at sites over the long-term is imperative for regional and local planning and responding to future sea-level rise," Walker told Rutgers Today. "By learning how different processes vary over time and contribute to sea-level change, we can more accurately estimate future contributions at specific sites."&lt;/p&gt;</div>

    </a>

<div aria-label="The Best Coffee Subscription Service" class="widget__image crop-16x9" data-runner-img-hd="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg2ODQ5NC9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY1NzE2MzMxM30.6_d6xjA3tVE1_mX86zf9Qas_bjsQC9vkzWRDA8w3MRs/img.jpg?width=1245&amp;quality=85&amp;coordinates=0%2C0%2C0%2C0&amp;height=700" data-runner-img-md="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg2ODQ5NC9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY1NzE2MzMxM30.6_d6xjA3tVE1_mX86zf9Qas_bjsQC9vkzWRDA8w3MRs/img.jpg?width=1245&amp;quality=85&amp;coordinates=0%2C0%2C0%2C0&amp;height=700" data-runner-img-sd="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg2ODQ5NC9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY1NzE2MzMxM30.6_d6xjA3tVE1_mX86zf9Qas_bjsQC9vkzWRDA8w3MRs/img.jpg?width=980&amp;quality=85" data-runner-style="padding-bottom: 56.25%;" data-type="image" role="img" style="padding-bottom: 56.25%;"><div class="lazyload-placeholder">

        ForsterForest / iStock / Getty Images
    </div><div class="body js-expandable clearfix js-listicle-body js-update-url css-listicle-body-2651187097" data-authors="Josh Hurst" data-elid="2651187097" data-headline="Best Organic and Specialty Coffee Subscriptions" data-post-url="https://www.ecowatch.com/best-organic-specialty-coffee-subscriptions-2651187097.html"><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>For coffee drinkers, there's really nothing more terrifying than the thought of waking up one morning and being all out of java. One way to ensure that never happens is to sign up for a coffee subscription service. This not only keeps you well-stocked, but it also gives you the opportunity to sample some high-quality and <a data-linked-post="2645140987" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/africa-organic-farming-2645140987.html" target="_blank">organic</a> coffee beans from around the world.<br/></p><p>Of course, like any <a data-linked-post="2649096829" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/healthy-energy-drinks-2649096829.html" target="_blank">specialty beverage</a> or product, a coffee subscription box should match your own preferences while also being good for people and the planet. In this article, we'll take a closer look at some of the top organic and specialty coffee subscription options on the market today.</p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>

&lt;a href="https://bulletproof.fdf2.net/vnnYzj" target="_blank"&gt;Bulletproof Coffee&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Best Coffee Selection - &lt;a href="https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=791106&amp;amp;u=2021263&amp;amp;m=62290&amp;amp;urllink=angelscup%2Ecom%2F&amp;amp;afftrack=EW%5FCoffeeSub" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Angels' Cup&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Best Carbon-Free Coffee - &lt;a href="https://groundsforchange.com/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Grounds for Change&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Best B Corp Coffee - &lt;a href="https://www.consciouscoffees.com/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Conscious Coffee&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Best for International Coffees - &lt;a href="https://atlascoffeeclub.com/" target="_blank"&gt;Atlas Coffee Club&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Best for Specialty Coffees - &lt;a href="https://beanbox.com/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Bean Box&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Best for Artisan Coffees - &lt;a href="https://www.mistobox.com/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Mistobox&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Most Eco-Friendly - &lt;a href="https://driftaway.coffee/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Driftaway Coffee&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Best Variety of Brewing Methods - &lt;a href="https://bluebottlecoffee.com/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Blue Bottle Coffee&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Most Affordable - &lt;a href="https://www.peets.com/pages/subscriptions" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Peet's Coffee&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Best for Home and Office - &lt;a href="https://crema.co/home" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Crema Coffee&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;h2&gt;How We Chose the Best Coffee Subscriptions&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p class="shortcode-media shortcode-media-rebelmouse-image"&gt;
        &lt;img class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" type="lazy-image" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg3NzQ5MC9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY1OTcyNDg2Nn0.eSobF1sc72Ax_ew8ovrY5VU33qdeVJ_D8nijDv62F44/img.jpg?width=980" id="b494f" width="1280" height="730" data-rm-shortcode-id="397b264ea87fcbac69ccb71421d83157" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"&gt;
        
        
        &lt;small class="image-media media-photo-credit" placeholder="Add Photo Credit..."&gt;Min Kim / Getty Images&lt;/small&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Before we get into specific recommendations, it may be helpful to note some of the criteria we used for making our assessment. Our ranking factors include:&lt;br&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Coffee Selection&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;Some subscription services do a better job than others of giving coffee lovers lots of options, not only allowing you to pick between different beans, but also allowing you to pick from whole bean vs. ground coffee. We also gave bonus points to subscription services that provide freshly-roasted craft coffee.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Subscription Options&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;Another important consideration is how much flexibility you have in your actual subscription. We love services that give you some choice in how much coffee you actually need, how often you wish to receive your next box, and the ability to try new flavors.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;USDA Organic/Fair Trade/Rainforest Alliance Certifications&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;Many coffee drinkers will want to verify that their purchase is Fair Trade and/or USDA organic certified. We looked for the best coffee subscriptions that make the environment and the people that grow their coffee a priority in sourcing. If they didn't have these certifications, we looked to see if they explained how they approached their sourcing instead.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Single-Origin Coffee&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;A lot of enthusiasts prefer single-origin coffee; that is, coffee made exclusively from beans grown in one specific geographic area. Single-origin coffee tends to provide unique characteristics and flavor notes that blended coffees cannot match.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Sustainability&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;If you're looking to minimize your environmental footprint then you'll definitely want to account for the sustainability practices of each subscription service. This can encompass the service's supply chain, production, packaging, and shipping.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Pricing&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;Naturally, one of the deciding factors in your organic coffee quest will be the price. Some subscriptions are more budget-friendly than others. We tried to select subscription options that that are affordable and still offer subscribers amazing coffee they can't find at the grocery store.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;The 12 Best Organic and Specialty Coffee Subscriptions&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p class="shortcode-media shortcode-media-rebelmouse-image"&gt;
        &lt;img class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" type="lazy-image" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg3NzUxNi9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYzNjA2ODc5M30.ZIj2xppNDdLmEyLwGr7hDktzWCUsZCp5PSCvG4NKEK0/img.jpg?width=980" id="d4746" width="1280" height="728" data-rm-shortcode-id="1f602e52d03b385192b19cf9bd782dd8" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"&gt;
        
        
        &lt;small class="image-media media-photo-credit" placeholder="Add Photo Credit..."&gt;RyanJLane / E+ / Getty Images&lt;/small&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="https://purity-coffee.fgjaok.net/rnnYgG" target="_blank"&gt;1.) Purity Coffee&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://purity-coffee.fgjaok.net/rnnYgG" target="_blank"&gt;Purity Coffee&lt;/a&gt; claims that their process maximizes the health benefits naturally found in coffee. They only use 100% USDA-certified organic coffee beans for all of their coffees. These are then screened for pesticides and molds, and then roasted using a special smokeless roasting process to ensure it contains the highest-possible levels of antioxidants. Subscribers can save on each order, and prepaid subscriptions receive free shipping.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Why buy: &lt;/strong&gt;Not only is Purity Coffee 100% organic, it's also sustainably sourced. They offer several specialty Founders' Roasts that are &lt;a href="https://www.rainforest-alliance.org/faqs/what-does-rainforest-alliance-certified-mean" target="_blank"&gt;Rainforest Alliance&lt;/a&gt;-certified and &lt;a href="https://nationalzoo.si.edu/migratory-birds/bird-friendly-coffee" target="_blank"&gt;Smithsonian Bird Friendly&lt;/a&gt;-certified for the grower's commitment to biodiversity and habitat conservation.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="https://bulletproof.fdf2.net/vnnYzj" target="_blank"&gt;2.) Bulletproof Coffee&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://bulletproof.fdf2.net/vnnYzj" target="_blank"&gt;Bulletproof Coffee&lt;/a&gt; is a keto coffee, or butter coffee, that contains both high-quality coffee and good fats to provide even more fuel to your mornings. It's meant to replace carb and sugar-heavy breakfasts while giving you what you need to get going. Bulletproof Coffee uses Rainforest Alliance-certified beans grown in direct partnership with farmers on high-altitude estates in Guatemala and Colombia. With their subscription option you can save 10% on each order, and receive free shipping on orders over $35.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Why buy: &lt;/strong&gt;Not only can Bulletproof Coffee change the way you start your day with a keto-friendly cup of coffee, but the coffee itself is grown using sustainable methods, is sustainably washed and mechanically dried, and then thoroughly tested for toxins and impurities.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=791106&amp;amp;u=2021263&amp;amp;m=62290&amp;amp;urllink=angelscup%2Ecom%2F&amp;amp;afftrack=EW%5FCoffeeSub" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;3.) Angels' Cup&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;If you're just getting into serious coffee consumption, or want to dip your toes into the subscription model, &lt;a href="https://shareasale.com/r.cfm?b=791106&amp;amp;u=2021263&amp;amp;m=62290&amp;amp;urllink=angelscup%2Ecom%2F&amp;amp;afftrack=EW%5FCoffeeSub" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Angels' Cup&lt;/a&gt; is an excellent starting point. You can begin by getting just a single 12 ounce bag of coffee, and they also offer blind sampler packs and subscriptions with different frequency levels, including weekly, twice monthly, or monthly. Their mobile app will help you discover the different tasting notes to find your favorites.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Why buy:&lt;/strong&gt; There's a lot of flexibility built into the Angels' Cup model, making it an ideal choice for those who are new to the gourmet coffee scene. While they don't source the coffees themselves, they do work with roasters who pay well-above Fair Trade prices.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="https://groundsforchange.com/" target="_blank"&gt;4.) Grounds for Change&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://groundsforchange.com/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Grounds for Change&lt;/a&gt; has a reputation for being one of the most progressive, stewardship-minded coffee companies out there. If you're looking for Fair Trade, organic, and/or carbon-free options, this certified B corp is where you can find them. They also showcase a lot of unique collections, from single-origin coffees to some enticing decaf options, that are well worth investigating. We're more than happy to include Grounds for Change on our list.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Why buy:&lt;/strong&gt; In terms of social responsibility, Grounds for Change can't be topped. They are the only company on our list that offers carbon-free coffee, meaning they offset 100% of the emissions from their coffees.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.consciouscoffees.com/" target="_blank"&gt;5.) Conscious Coffee&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.consciouscoffees.com/" target="_blank"&gt;Conscious Coffee&lt;/a&gt; has made some really admirable investments in coffee-growing communities across the world. Their model of sustainability and corporate responsibility is commendable, but they are equally passionate about exquisite roasting. They belong on our list for these reasons and so many more, including their emphasis on 100 percent organic coffee, small-batch freshness, and sustainable sourcing.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Why buy: &lt;/strong&gt;Conscious Coffee sets a high bar for stewardship and responsibility. We strongly recommend them to anyone who wants to invest in sustainable coffee-farming across the world.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="https://atlascoffeeclub.com/" target="_blank"&gt;6.) Atlas Coffee Club&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;One of the many reasons to consider a subscription coffee service is that it will give you a chance to explore different flavors from around the world. And there is no subscription service that serves up international variety quite like &lt;a href="https://atlascoffeeclub.com/" target="_blank"&gt;Atlas Coffee Club&lt;/a&gt;. Each month, you'll get a new coffee from a different country like Costa Rica, Colombia, or Ethiopia, in a bag that's modeled after indigenous textiles or local landscapes. For anyone who loves to travel or simply likes to try new things, Atlas Coffee Club offers a truly transportive experience.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Why buy:&lt;/strong&gt; There's no better option for trying out different coffee flavors from across cultures. The company also pays well above market prices to growers to support ethically sustainable farming practices.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="https://beanbox.com/" target="_blank"&gt;7.) Bean Box&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://beanbox.com/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Bean Box&lt;/a&gt; is another outstanding choice for java enthusiasts who are curious to sample different tastes. Based in Seattle, Bean Box partners with different coffee roasters from around the world, including small-batch, independent roasters from the U.S., South America, Africa, and beyond. They'll send you a different blend each month, allowing you to develop a really broad and sophisticated palette. We also really love the price point on this one, which offers a great value.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Why buy: &lt;/strong&gt;If you're looking for a budget-friendly way to sample specialty coffees, Bean Box is a great coffee subscription service to consider.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.mistobox.com/" target="_blank"&gt;8.) Mistobox&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;If you're attempting to maximize your coffee variety, you'll probably be over the moon about &lt;a href="https://www.mistobox.com/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Mistobox&lt;/a&gt;. This coffee subscription company boasts partnerships with more than 50 roasters across the world, which is all but unparalleled. We also recommend them due to their commitment to Fair Trade and ecologically sustainable practices. Mistobox has a coffee curation service that will help you determine just where to start. So, if you feel overwhelmed by all the different organic coffee options, Mistobox has you covered.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Why buy:&lt;/strong&gt; We recommend Mistobox for their sustainability, their corporate citizenship, their sheer variety of organic coffees, and their curation options.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="https://driftaway.coffee/" target="_blank"&gt;9.) Driftaway Coffee&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;With &lt;a href="https://driftaway.coffee/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Driftaway Coffee&lt;/a&gt;, the name of the game is personalization. Their service will actually enable you to establish "coffee profiles," pinpointing your tastes and helping them determine exactly what to send you each month. As if that weren't enough, Driftaway guarantees single-source whole bean coffees, and they also do an exemplary job of providing compostable packaging. Finally, they have a sustainability program that supports regional farmers.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Why buy: &lt;/strong&gt;A great pick for single-origin whole bean coffee, and also a really great model for sustainability within the single-origin coffee subscription vertical.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="https://bluebottlecoffee.com/" target="_blank"&gt;10.) Blue Bottle Coffee&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;If you really want your coffee to be as fresh as can be, then we heartily recommend &lt;a href="https://bluebottlecoffee.com/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Blue Bottle&lt;/a&gt;. They ship everything within 48 hours of roasting, ensuring you get the most vibrant flavors. Another thing we'll mention about this organic coffee subscription service is that they provide a lot of different options for espresso, decaf, single-origin, and blended coffees. There's definitely a lot to like here, especially if you're keen on small-batch coffee.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Why buy: &lt;/strong&gt;For fresh flavors and plenty of variety, Blue Bottle Coffee is a great choice. The majority of their coffees are certified organic, and they pay at least Fair Trade prices to growers, often more.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.peets.com/pages/subscriptions" target="_blank"&gt;11.) Peet's Coffee&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.peets.com/pages/subscriptions" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Peet's Coffee&lt;/a&gt; has a ton of great products to consider, including some eclectic subscription options. You can take your pick between their small batch series, single-origin coffees, signature blends, and beyond. What's more, they boast plenty of flexibility with scheduling, making it easy to get coffee exactly when you need it. Plus they offer free shipping on coffee subscriptions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Why buy: &lt;/strong&gt;Peet's is an outstanding choice for anyone seeking plenty of variety and built-in flexibility. You may recognize them from the grocery store, but this brand is seriously committed to responsible sourcing, support for local farmers, and energy-efficient roasting.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href="https://crema.co/" target="_blank"&gt;12.) Crema.co&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://crema.co/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Crema Coffee&lt;/a&gt; is a popular choice among coffee connoisseurs, and it's not hard to understand why. There are over 450 coffees to choose from, spanning roasters located all over the world. You can customize your subscription to make certain you only get the roasts you're really going to be into, and you can even rate coffees to help keep track of your tastes. Crema Coffee offers subscription packages for your household and for your workplace.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Why buy: &lt;/strong&gt;Crema Coffee offers incredible variety, plenty of options for personalization, and even a subscription model for your office. They ensure that they only work with roasters committed to an ethical coffee supply chain.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;How Does a Coffee Subscription Work?&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p class="shortcode-media shortcode-media-rebelmouse-image"&gt;
        &lt;img class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" type="lazy-image" data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg3NzUyOC9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY2ODE5NDkyMX0.xt8n0DvBOdjtdjPhFklkR6hzkpOpt_itM_9xGlKCCJ0/img.jpg?width=980" id="f1260" width="1280" height="723" data-rm-shortcode-id="205f867f832ca47b447a4e86b239776b" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"&gt;
        
        
        &lt;small class="image-media media-photo-credit focus-visible" data-focus-visible-added="" placeholder="Add Photo Credit..."&gt;amenic181 / iStock / Getty Images Plus&lt;/small&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Clearly, there are plenty of options to choose from as you seek a subscription-based coffee delivery service. But if you're new to this whole concept, you may have some lingering questions about precisely what you can expect from your coffee subscription.&lt;br&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;First of all, keep in mind that these subscriptions all work a little bit differently. Most of the companies on our list offer a coffee of the month club and provide different coffees to try with each delivery.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For a general overview of the coffee subscription process, though, you can typically expect something a bit like this:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Select the Type of Subscription You Want&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Are you looking to get just a sampler of coffee beans each month? Or do you want to stay well-supplied, with new coffees arriving more frequently? Choosing your preferred subscription model is usually the first step.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Choose What Kind of Coffee You Want&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Different subscription services will allow you different levels of customization, but there is always some way of indicating your preferences, whether you like dark roasts over light roasts, single-origin coffees over blends, etc.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Get Coffee Delivered to You&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Most coffee subscription services will box your coffee in recyclable/compostable materials and deliver right to your front door. Because it's so important to maintain freshness, most subscription companies ship within a day or two of roasting.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Prepare Your Coffee&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Note that, with whole bean options, you'll actually need a grinder to grind your coffee; if you choose ground coffee, then it will be ready to brew as soon as it shows up at your door.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Try New Types of Coffee&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Finally, note that subscription coffee companies tend to rotate their roaster throughout the year. Make sure you explore some different options, and you might just discover your next favorite coffee!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;Coffee Subscription FAQ&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;h3&gt;What is Fair Trade coffee?&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;We've highlighted the importance of Fair Trade coffee, but what exactly does this term mean? Essentially, when you buy Fair Trade coffee, it means that you are directly supporting local coffee-growing families in the developing world. More specifically, Fair Trade denotes a commitment to fair prices, community development efforts, and good stewardship of the environment. The Fair Trade designation is an important way to verify that you're getting ethically-sourced coffee beans. Fair Trade sets a floor on prices that allow coffee farmers to make a living, and many specialty coffee roasters pay much more than Fair Trade prices to local growers.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;How is Organic Coffee Grown?&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;Another common question: What does it mean for coffee to be USDA-certified as organic? Fundamentally, organic coffee is grown without the use of any artificial chemicals, including prohibited pesticides and herbicides. To achieve the official USDA certification, a coffee must be at least 95 percent organic. Growers in certain regions may have trouble attaining this certification for various reasons, but specialty roasters typically seek to support sustainable farming practices and supply chains.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h3&gt;What is Single-Origin Coffee?&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;Single-origin coffee refers to a coffee made with beans that are all grown in one specific region. This type of coffee offers some really unique flavors and characteristics. The alternative is blended coffee, which may mix beans that come from a multiple places. Many coffee enthusiasts prefer the purity of single-origin, though of course, this is all a matter of personal preference.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;Order Your Coffee Subscription Today&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;Looking for a way to get organic, Fair Trade coffee delivered straight to your front door? There are plenty of subscription models that will do just that, all while letting you sample some incredible beans from across the world.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Take a look at the options we've listed here, and look for the coffee subscription service that seems like it's best aligned with your tastes and your budget. And from there, just sit back and wait for your next bag of coffee beans to show up at your home or office.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Josh Hurst &lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/em&gt;&lt;em&gt;is a journalist, critic, and essayist. He lives in Knoxville, TN, with his wife and three sons. He covers natural health, nutrition, supplements, and clean energy. His writing has appeared in Health, Shape, and Remedy Review.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;<div class="around-the-web"><div class="from-your-site__headline">From Your Site Articles</div>

"adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>At least five people have died in a <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/tornadoes" target="_self">tornado</a> outbreak that roared across the U.S. South Thursday and Friday, destroying homes and downing power lines. </p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tornado-alabama-georgia" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651223167" data-published-at="1616776533" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;As many as eight tornadoes may have touched down in the state of Alabama on Thursday, Birmingham National Weather Service (NWS) meteorologist John De Block told &lt;a href="https://www.al.com/news/2021/03/shelby-county-storm-damage-no-injuries-reported-buildings-damaged-us-280-blocked-by-trees.html" target="_blank"&gt;AL.com&lt;/a&gt;. One of them travelled around 100 miles across the state. The deadliest scythed diagonally through the rural Calhoun County.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Five people lost their lives and for those families, it will never be the same," Calhoun County Sheriff Matthew Wade said at a Thursday evening briefing reported by &lt;a href="https://apnews.com/article/alabama-georgia-tornadoes-weather-storms-620d416ec174e1038182ff1483003197" target="_blank"&gt;The Associated Press&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tornado-alabama-georgia" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651223167" data-published-at="1616776533" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;div id="2bcac" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="a44cc8ed9581d4e6f6a2d96cd00b66c3"&gt;&lt;blockquote class="twitter-tweet twitter-custom-tweet" data-twitter-tweet-id="1375175854980993025" data-partner="rebelmouse"&gt;&lt;div style="margin:1em 0"&gt;Long lived supercell continues to produce a tornado in northern Calhoun County. Radar confirmed tornado will move j… https://t.co/YbpIBwDmXy&lt;/div&gt; &amp;mdash; NWS Birmingham (@NWS Birmingham)&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/NWSBirmingham/statuses/1375175854980993025"&gt;1616702448.0&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;/div&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tornado-alabama-georgia" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651223167" data-published-at="1616776533" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;p&gt;The tornadoes also caused injuries and extensive damage, including in the counties around Birmingham.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In the city of Pelham, 60 homes were damaged, 22 of them majorly, AL.com reported. Rick Partridge, who lives with his wife in the Cahaba Valleys Estates community in Pelham, said more than a dozen homes in the community were damaged or destroyed.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"It was horrible," Partridge said. "It didn't take 10 seconds."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The storms also wreaked havoc on an airport in Centreville.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Airplanes strewn like toys, it was unreal," Centreville Mayor Mike Oakley told AL.com.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tornado-alabama-georgia" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651223167" data-published-at="1616776533" id="rebelltitem4">&lt;p&gt;Alabama Emergency Management Agency Director Brian Hastings estimated that the number of homes damaged or destroyed across the state was in the hundreds, as &lt;a href="https://www.npr.org/2021/03/25/981321584/tornado-strikes-alabama-severe-weather-lashes-southern-states" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;NPR reported&lt;/a&gt;. At the height of the storms, around 30,000 people were without power.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;De Block said the Alabama tornadoes were part of a "super cell" that later moved on to Georgia. A tornado likely touched down in the city of Newman, which is located southwest of Atlanta, around midnight Friday, NPR reported. The storm downed power lines and knocked out power for around 5,000 people, according to The Associated Press. It damaged buildings, including Newman High School.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Crews tell me they've never seen a storm cause this much damage here," Atlanta-based journalist Sabrina Silva &lt;a href="https://twitter.com/SabSilv/status/1375367921023746050?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw%7Ctwcamp%5Etweetembed%7Ctwterm%5E1375367921023746050%7Ctwgr%5E%7Ctwcon%5Es1_&amp;amp;ref_url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.npr.org%2F2021%2F03%2F25%2F981321584%2Ftornado-strikes-alabama-severe-weather-lashes-southern-states" target="_blank"&gt;tweeted&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tornado-alabama-georgia" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651223167" data-published-at="1616776533" id="rebelltitem5">&lt;div id="5ce7b" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="ff22d1ea5d205314dddd127093a01c41"&gt;&lt;blockquote class="twitter-tweet twitter-custom-tweet" data-twitter-tweet-id="1375367921023746050" data-partner="rebelmouse"&gt;&lt;div style="margin:1em 0"&gt;The storm severely damaged parts of Newnan High School. 

Crews tell me they’ve never seen a storm cause this much… https://t.co/kwxru9at2d&lt;/div&gt; &amp;mdash; Sabrina Silva (@Sabrina Silva)&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/SabSilv/statuses/1375367921023746050"&gt;1616748240.0&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;/div&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-6" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tornado-alabama-georgia" data-id="6" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651223167" data-published-at="1616776533" id="rebelltitem6">&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/extreme-weather" target="_self"&gt;Extreme weather&lt;/a&gt; lashed a large swathe of the South, threatening flooding and thunderstorms in Tennessee, Kentucky and the Carolinas, as The Associated Press reported. In Ohio, thunderstorms knocked out power for more than 100,000 people.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;There is &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/lee-county-alabama-tornado-2630610008.html" target="_self"&gt;evidence&lt;/a&gt; that the traditional "tornado alley" is shifting east, away from the Great Plains and towards the U.S. South. This makes tornadoes deadlier, since the South is more populated and people are more likely to live in vulnerable mobile homes. In addition, tornadoes in the region often strike at night. There is some evidence that the &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change/" target="_self"&gt;climate crisis&lt;/a&gt; is behind the shift.&lt;/p&gt;</div>

"order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>"How America's most endangered cat could help save Florida."</p><p>As its headline promises, <a href="https://www.nationalgeographic.com/magazine/article/florida-panthers-return-imperiled-by-development-feature" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">National Geographic's latest feature</a> on the endangered Florida panther explores the unspoken, symbiotic relationship between the big cats and the humans they must coexist with. The article also showcases intimate, rare photographs of the panthers, which took five years to capture. </p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/endangered-panther-florida" data-id="1" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651221929" data-published-at="1616775718" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;According to the &lt;a href="https://www.nwf.org/Educational-Resources/Wildlife-Guide/Mammals/Florida-Panther#:~:text=Florida%20panthers%20are%20about%20six,the%20southwestern%20tip%20of%20Florida." rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;National Wildlife Federation (NWF)&lt;/a&gt;, Florida panthers are actually a subspecies of mountain lion — the only one remaining in the Eastern U.S. They're also known as pumas and cougars. The subspecies' historic range once extended from Florida to Louisiana throughout the Gulf Coast states, and even Arkansas, NWF reported. Today, wild Florida panthers can only be found in southwestern Florida.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Hunting decimated the population, and the species was among the first to be added to the U.S. &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/endangered-species" target="_self"&gt;endangered species&lt;/a&gt; list in 1973, with fewer than 30 individuals remaining, according to the National Geographic article. Habitat loss compounded the issue. With such a small population, inbreeding, which could lead to diseases and genetic malfunctions, was of particular concern. Journalist Douglas Main wrote the feature story, and he shared in a &lt;a href="https://twitter.com/Douglas_Main/status/1369312122879041538" target="_blank"&gt;twitter thread&lt;/a&gt; how many people feared that Florida's panther had gone, or would soon go extinct, during that decade.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A massive &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/conservation" target="_self"&gt;conservation&lt;/a&gt; effort ensued, including bringing in eight Texas mountain lions to breed with the native Florida population in order to inject fresh genetic diversity into the population, Main said.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;However, the subspecies is still so critically endangered that it remains vulnerable to "just about every major threat," NWF reported. Habitat loss is the biggest obstacle.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/endangered-panther-florida" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651221929" data-published-at="1616775718" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;p&gt;According to the &lt;a href="https://www.fws.gov/southeast/wildlife/mammals/florida-panther/" target="_blank"&gt;U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service (FWS)&lt;/a&gt;, Florida panthers require large, contiguous areas of suitable land to live on. They are solitary and roam widely in order to meet their social, reproductive and energetic needs, FWS reported. Unfortunately, they are still restricted to less than five percent of their historical range, the report noted.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;As more people move to Florida, continued development threatens the little remaining open land and panther habitat. For panthers, this is a huge challenge to recovery, and has increased cat-on-cat territorial spats and car collisions — the leading causes of death, National Geographic reported. About 25 Florida panthers are killed annually by vehicles, a devastating blow to a tiny population and "a reflection of how development and road construction threaten the species at a time when roughly 900 people are moving to Florida every day," the story detailed.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The conservation efforts worked to save the panther from the brink of extinction, but they're still very much at risk, said National Geographic Explorer Carlton Ward Jr. Ward is an eighth generation Floridian and habitat protection advocate, as well as the photographer who spent five years capturing the panther images for the feature.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-8" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/endangered-panther-florida" data-id="8" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651221929" data-published-at="1616776411" id="rebelltitem8">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"
            data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg4MjA3NS9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYxODU2ODAwOH0.aArp5UJ6jncOIZYy4ZTy1x7erEh9THz-GA9XnDtMMTE/img.jpg?width=980"
            id="876c7"
            width="5310"
            height="3908"
            data-rm-shortcode-id="ff716ddc464a92e619be47b854836d6b" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p>A male panther leaps over a creek at Florida Panther National Wildlife Refuge in southwestern Florida. The rarely seen cats, which number only around 200, are reclaiming territory north of the Everglades, but their habitat is threatened by encroaching suburban sprawl. Carlton Ward, Jr.</p></small></div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/endangered-panther-florida" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651221929" data-published-at="1616775718" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;p&gt;For Ward, it became an obsession to document the elusive, endangered cats, and the pictures reflect that. "The lead image for the story, a panther jumping across a log around a flooded section of swamp, that picture took two years to capture," he admitted.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For five years, Ward set up state-of-the-art camera traps throughout the Florida woods and swamps. He shared with EcoWatch what he learned about the need to continue balancing Florida's tremendous population growth with conserving the iconic species.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"We need to cultivate a culture of coexistence," Ward said. "If the panther goes extinct, I will be worried about all the other wildlife and people in Florida, because it means we will have missed the opportunity we have now to &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/land-conservation" target="_self"&gt;conserve enough land&lt;/a&gt; to ensure balance between wildlife and people."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Today, the panther population has grown to roughly 200, and Ward's photos show that the cats are moving northward to reclaim old territories. This is critical, because northward expansion is the only path for long-term survival, Main wrote in National Geographic.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/endangered-panther-florida" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651221929" data-published-at="1616775718" id="rebelltitem5">&lt;p&gt;"The southern tip of Florida is not enough land to sustain a genetically viable, resilient population of panthers," Ward told EcoWatch. "The cats can only continue moving north if the Florida Wildlife Corridor, a patchwork of &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/public-lands" target="_self"&gt;public&lt;/a&gt; and private lands that run through the state, is preserved. The Florida Wildlife Corridor is the lifeline and path of recovery for panthers."&lt;br&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Yet this requires the participation of landowners and ranchers, who need more conservation funding to prevent their open spaces from becoming subdivisions, parking lots and roads, Main explained in the story. Conservation easements use up development rights while allowing the owners to continue farming and ranching, Main said.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"The land is still there. We have a moment right now where we can choose to conserve," Ward told EcoWatch. "Hundreds of landowners are open to conservation as an alternative to development. They're waiting for conservation easements or to sell their land for national parks. We need to meet this opportunity."&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-7" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/endangered-panther-florida" data-id="7" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651221929" data-published-at="1616775718" id="rebelltitem7">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"
            data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg4MjAxNC9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY1NTQwMDk1NH0.s9rj71gsCGmEDOaigPtt5WSIdD8_bWcDQbS-Gxh9-_4/img.jpg?width=980"
            id="16e2f"
            width="4000"
            height="2667"
            data-rm-shortcode-id="cdea1174d964f9221eec68291a062647" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p>Wildlife veterinarian Lara Cusack handles more kittens belonging to FP224. These young cats were measured and given immunity boosters while their mother was hunting away from the den. When panthers have space and protected habitats, their populations can grow. Only about one in three Florida panther kittens survives to adulthood. Carlton Ward Jr. / National Geographic Society</p></small></div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-6" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/endangered-panther-florida" data-id="6" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651221929" data-published-at="1616775718" id="rebelltitem6">&lt;p&gt;Landowners and ranchers, who were traditionally pitted against panthers when their cattle were eaten, will also benefit from increased protections for the cats. "On the Endangered Species Act, do you see 'cowboy' or 'rancher' written on it? No, but we benefit from the protections afforded the panther," Main quoted Florida rancher Elton Langford. "Both share a common enemy: Development," Main wrote.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;People with multi-generational connections to the land share something in common with a species that's lived there for 20,000 years, Ward said. Both need the land to remain intact and open.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"There is common ground and common threat and common opportunity," Ward concluded. "That's where I feel the most hope — in how much common ground there is in saving a species, helping sustain a way of life and in sustaining the headwaters of the Everglades and the water supply. The panther is a great icon for everyone to conserve all of this."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For more on this story, visit &lt;a href="https://www.nationalgeographic.com/magazine/article/florida-panthers-return-imperiled-by-development-feature" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;National Geographic&lt;/a&gt;. The story appears in print in National Geographic's April 2021 issue.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-9" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/endangered-panther-florida" data-id="9" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651221929" data-published-at="1616785341" id="rebelltitem9">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"

<h6 class="widget__headline h6">
<a aria-label="U.S. Military Ordered 'Clandestine Burning' of Toxic Chemicals in Low-Income Neighborhoods, Study Finds" class="widget__headline-text custom-post-headline" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/military-burning-toxic-chemicals-neighborhoods-2651221968.html">
        U.S. Military Ordered 'Clandestine Burning' of Toxic Chemicals in Low-Income Neighborhoods, Study Finds
    </a>
</h6>
<div class="social-author clearfix">
<div class="social-author__avatar image">

"\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_8_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 8}, {"amp": "\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_9_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_9_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>By Kenny Stancil</p><p>New <a href="https://www.bennington.edu/center-advancement-of-public-action/environment-and-public-action/understanding-pfoa" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">research </a>conducted by environmental justice scholars at Vermont's Bennington College reveals that between 2016 and 2020, the U.S. military oversaw the "<a href="https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2021/mar/25/us-military-toxic-chemicals-us-states" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">clandestine burning</a>" of more than 20 million pounds of Aqueous Fire Fighting Foam in low-income communities around the country — even though there is no evidence that incineration destroys the toxic "<a href="https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/forever-chemicals-are-widespread-in-u-s-drinking-water/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">forever chemicals</a>" that make up the foam and are linked to a range of cancers, developmental disorders, immune dysfunction, and infertility.</p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/military-burning-toxic-chemicals-neighborhoods" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651221968" data-published-at="1616768294" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;"In defiance of common sense and environmental expertise, the Department of Defense (DOD) has enlisted poor communities across the U.S. as unwilling test subjects in its toxic experiment with burning AFFF," David Bond, associate director of the Center for the Advancement of Public Action at Bennington College, &lt;a href="https://www.bennington.edu/sites/default/files/sources/docs/AFFF%20News%20Release%20%5B03.23.21%5D.pdf" target="_blank"&gt;said&lt;/a&gt; in a statement earlier this week.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Noting that scientists, the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency (EPA), and even Pentagon officials have warned that "burning AFFF is an unproven method and dangerous mix that threatens the health of millions of Americans," Bond characterized the &lt;a href="https://theintercept.com/2019/01/27/toxic-firefighting-foam-pfas-pfoa/" target="_blank"&gt;decision&lt;/a&gt; of the military to dump huge stockpiles of AFFF and AFFF wastewater into "a handful of habitually negligent incinerators" as a "harebrained" operation as well as a manifestation of environmental injustice.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/military-burning-toxic-chemicals-neighborhoods" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651221968" data-published-at="1616768294" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;p&gt;"In effect," he added, "the Pentagon redistributed its AFFF problem into poor and working-class neighborhoods."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;After months of compiling and analyzing &lt;a href="https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1bqawpCZWFGXq725XzZ6G5OdAJjkyuHwIVmKBjl3iwKc/edit#gid=1266910885" target="_blank"&gt;data&lt;/a&gt; — obtained last year from the Pentagon and the New York State Department of Environmental Conservation — the team from Vermont launched an &lt;a href="https://www.bennington.edu/afff" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;interactive website&lt;/a&gt; this week that publicizes for the first time the results of their investigation into all known shipments of AFFF to hazardous waste incinerators in the U.S.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/military-burning-toxic-chemicals-neighborhoods" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651221968" data-published-at="1616768294" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;p&gt;The Bennington College researchers summarized their findings as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;Over 20 million pounds of the toxic firefighting foam AFFF and AFFF wastewater was incinerated between 2016-2020;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;The U.S. military, the EPA, and state regulators all expressed serious concern about the ability of incineration to destroy the toxic chemicals in AFFF during this time;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Six incinerators were contracted to burn AFFF. Each is a habitual violator of environmental law. Since 2017, three of the incinerators were out of compliance with environmental law 100% of the time while the other incinerators were out of compliance with environmental law about 50% of the time;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;35% of known shipments of AFFF (7.7 million pounds) was burned at the Norlite Hazardous Waste Incinerator in Cohoes, New York, located within a densely populated urban area and less than 400 feet from a public housing complex. Norlite burned 2.47 million pounds of AFFF and 5.3 million pounds of AFFF wastewater, which likely was burned in violation of its Resource Conservation and Recovery Act permit;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;40% of the national stockpile of AFFF (5.5 million pounds) was sent to "fuel-blending" facilities where it was mixed into fuels for industrial use. It is not clear where the AFFF-laden fuel went next, although the DOD contract stipulates incineration should be the endpoint; and&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;970,000 pounds of AFFF was burned overseas.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/military-burning-toxic-chemicals-neighborhoods" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651221968" data-published-at="1616768294" id="rebelltitem4">&lt;p&gt;AFFF contains contaminants known as perfluoroalkyl and polyfluoroalkyl substances (PFAS); exposure to trace amounts of these synthetic chemicals is associated with a variety of detrimental health effects, and some have &lt;a href="https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2021/mar/18/toxic-chemicals-health-humanity-erin-brokovich" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;argued&lt;/a&gt; that PFAS are so risky that they not only endanger public health but threaten to undermine human reproduction writ large.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Jane Williams, chair of the Sierra Club's National Clean Air team &lt;a href="https://www.bennington.edu/sites/default/files/sources/docs/AFFF%20News%20Release%20%5B03.23.21%5D.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;stressed&lt;/a&gt;: "We simply must stop burning PFAS compounds."&lt;br&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Attempting to burn these forever chemicals can generate highly toxic emissions which endanger the health of nearby communities," she said. "Burning also releases gases which are powerful climate forcing chemicals."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;According to Williams, "EPA and DOD are both pursuing advanced technologies that can more effectively destroy these compounds without causing these unacceptable impacts."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The pursuit of alternative disposal methods raises the question, posed by the researchers on their website: "If incineration is an unproven means of destroying these toxins, is burning AFFF solving the problem or simply emitting it into the poor communities that so often surround incinerators in the U.S.?"&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;According to the researchers, the military rushed to burn more than 20 million pounds of AFFF over the past four years because they feared the substance "would be classified as a toxic chemical (and with that designation, would require new safeguards and introduce new liability)."&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/military-burning-toxic-chemicals-neighborhoods" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651221968" data-published-at="1616768294" id="rebelltitem5">&lt;p&gt;In a column published Thursday in The Guardian, Bond &lt;a href="https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2021/mar/25/us-military-toxic-chemicals-us-states" target="_blank"&gt;explained&lt;/a&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;While some states file suit against the manufactures of AFFF, the fingerprints of the U.S. Armed Forces are all over the scene of the crime. When federal scientists moved to publish a comprehensive review of the toxic chemistry of AFFF in 2018, DOD officials called that science "&lt;a href="https://s3.amazonaws.com/ucs-documents/science-and-democracy/PFAS-CDC-study-2.pdf" target="_blank"&gt;a public relations nightmare&lt;/a&gt;" and tried to &lt;a href="https://blog.ucsusa.org/michael-halpern/bipartisan-outrage-as-epa-white-house-try-to-cover-up-chemical-health-assessment" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;suppress the findings&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;Beyond damning internal emails, the military is still in possession of a tremendous amount of AFFF. As the EPA and states around the U.S. begin to designate &lt;a href="https://news.bloomberglaw.com/product-liability-and-toxics-law/toxic-firefighting-foam-with-pfas-scrutinized-by-multiple-states?context=article-related" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;AFFF a hazardous substance&lt;/a&gt;, the military's stockpiles of AFFF are starting to add up to an astronomical liability on the military's balance sheet. Perhaps thinking the Trump administration presented an opportune moment, the Pentagon decided to torch their AFFF problem in 2016.&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;Despite AFFF's extraordinary resistance to fire, incineration quietly became the military's preferred method to handle AFFF. "&lt;a href="https://www.dla.mil/Portals/104/Documents/DispositionServices/Library/SEPT2017NewsletterFINAL.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;We knew that this would be a costly endeavor, since it meant we'd be burning something that was engineered to put out fires&lt;/a&gt;," Steve Schneider, chief of Hazardous Disposal for the logistics wing of DOD, said in 2017 as the operation got underway.&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;---&lt;br&gt;&lt;br&gt;As the military was sending AFFF to incinerators around the country, the EPA, state regulators, and university scientists all warned that subjecting AFFF to extremely high temperatures would likely conjure up &lt;a href="https://cfpub.epa.gov/si/si_public_file_download.cfm?p_download_id=539774&amp;amp;Lab=CEMM" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;a witches brew of fluorinated toxins&lt;/a&gt;, that existing smokestack technologies would be &lt;a href="https://cfpub.epa.gov/si/si_public_record_Report.cfm?dirEntryId=348571&amp;amp;Lab=CESER" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;insufficient to monitor poisonous emissions&lt;/a&gt; let alone capture them, and that &lt;a href="https://theintercept.com/2020/04/28/toxic-pfas-afff-upstate-new-york/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;dangerous chemicals might rain down&lt;/a&gt; on surrounding neighborhoods. Weighing out its own liability against the health of these communities, the Pentagon struck the match.&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Judith Enck, former EPA regional administrator, &lt;a href="https://www.bennington.edu/sites/default/files/sources/docs/AFFF%20News%20Release%20%5B03.23.21%5D.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;said&lt;/a&gt; the data compiled by the Bennington College team demonstrate that "we have a national problem on our hands."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Congress needs to throw cold water on the Pentagon's mad dash to burn toxic firefighting foam. There is no evidence that incineration destroys AFFF," she added, calling for "a national ban on burning these forever chemicals."&lt;/p&gt;</div>
