true, "new_amp": "\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_9_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>By Tara Lohan</p><p>European green crabs arrived on the eastern shores of North America in the early 1800s, likely as ship ballast stowaways or affixed to boat hulls. They found their way to the continent's western shores by the 1980s, and they've caused trouble in every new ecosystem they invade. </p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/invasive-species-management" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651221690" data-published-at="1616766506" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;Wherever green crabs (&lt;em&gt;Carcinus maenas&lt;/em&gt;) land, scientists have documented them decimating food webs by devouring benthic invertebrates that provide nourishment for shorebirds, fishes and other species. Over the years, they have eaten their way onto a list of the world's top &lt;a href="https://www.dfo-mpo.gc.ca/species-especes/profiles-profils/europeangreencrab-crabevert-eng.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;10 most unwanted species&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The economic toll of their appetite is large, too. European green crabs were estimated to have caused $22 million in damage a year to the East Coast commercial shellfishery alone.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Causing both ecological and economic harm has put green crabs in the spotlight, and a team of researchers from the University of California, Davis and other institutions have been studying how to best eradicate them. Along the way the scientists made a surprising discovery that they believe could change how managers deal with other invasive aquatic species.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h1&gt;Green Crab Revelations&lt;/h1&gt;&lt;p&gt;In 2009 the researchers decided to see if they could eradicate the invasive species from a small area where the crabs had newly arrived — the Seadrift Lagoon in Stinson Beach, California, about half an hour from San Francisco's Golden Gate Bridge.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"We thought we could undertake this kind of proof of concept to determine how many bodies, how many traps and how much effort it would take to get rid of the green crab in a fairly small, contained area," says one of those researchers, &lt;a href="https://desp.ucdavis.edu/people/edwin-grosholz" target="_blank"&gt;Edwin (Ted) Grosholz&lt;/a&gt;, a professor at U.C. Davis.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;They were successful at reducing the population by more than 90% — from 125,000 crabs in 2009 to fewer than 10,000 by 2013. "We were feeling very good with ourselves," he says, "But then suddenly the population exploded, and we were faced with even more crabs."&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/invasive-species-management" data-id="2" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651221690" data-published-at="1616766506" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"
            data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg4MTMxNi9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY2NjY3MjgzOX0.WzI8ZrC2mKsHG1YyidwLuQ_LuhAAwJhD_ZNR4fvj5_k/img.jpg?width=980"
            id="1f787"
            width="800"
            height="600"
            data-rm-shortcode-id="693990fc169aac11c73a1d7411a801c9" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p>Catching invasive European green crabs. USFWS</p></small></div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/invasive-species-management" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651221690" data-published-at="1616766506" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;p&gt;By 2014 the number of green crabs in Seadrift Lagoon shot up to an alarming 300,000. Other nearby bays didn't experience a similar population explosion, leaving the researchers wondering what the heck could have caused it.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;It turns out that this rather counterintuitive ecological response — where removal efforts can trigger a steep population rebound — had been found in theoretical models, uncontrolled studies and anecdotal reports for decades. "But we were the first who showed in an experiment with controls that in fact, this can happen, it did happen," says Grosholz.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The reason why they believe the population took off? Quite simply, green crabs are cannibalistic. Adults keep the population in check by eating some of the youngsters. But traps to eradicate the crabs caught only the adults, which left a slew of uneaten offspring ready to grow big and strong.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Given time things could have gotten even worse, as a female green crab that reaches maturity can produce up to 185,000 eggs.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;These findings revealed important data for managing invasive European green crabs, which have now made their way to five continents, but the researchers believe the implications go far beyond one species.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"The results of this study provide an urgent warning to those involved in the management of invasive species," they write in a &lt;a href="https://www.pnas.org/content/118/12/e2003955118" target="_blank"&gt;new study&lt;/a&gt; in the &lt;em&gt;Proceedings of National Academy of Sciences&lt;/em&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/invasive-species-management" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651221690" data-published-at="1616766506" id="rebelltitem4">&lt;h1&gt;Bigger Lessons&lt;/h1&gt;&lt;p&gt;The factors that led to the population explosion — known as the hydra effect — aren't unique to European green crabs. It could happen with other aquatic species, too, says Grosholz, including almost all crabs, lobsters, shrimp, and even a number of fishes.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;And it's not just species that eat their young, either. "You can see this response in any species where the adults consume a lot of the resources that their offspring might use," he says.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Their findings, he says, suggest that ecologists and managers may need to rethink how they manage invasive species that fit these criteria.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"The bigger picture is that there are people all over the planet spending a lot of money trying to eradicate invasive species — in marine ecosystems in particular — and our message here is to stop, back away," he says. "Let's give up trying to fully eradicate these types of species."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A better idea, he says, is to reduce the species down to a lower level where the harm they cause is eliminated or reduced, but not so low that the species have an opportunity bounce back.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Another recent &lt;a href="https://esajournals.onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1002/fee.2277" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;study&lt;/a&gt; in the journal &lt;em&gt;Frontiers in Ecology and the Environment,&lt;/em&gt; by Grosholz and University of Alberta biologist &lt;a href="https://apps.ualberta.ca/directory/person/sgreen1" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Stephanie J. Green&lt;/a&gt;, lays out how to undertake this strategy of "functional eradication."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Grosholz and Green surveyed more than 200 aquatic invasive-species specialists about how they try to manage invasive species and whether they focus on eradication, containment or suppression. What was most interesting, says Grosholz, was that virtually none had specific population targets for the invasive species they were managing.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"It's either 'we're going to go get them all' or 'we're going to try to knock the population down,' but they don't have any specific number," he explains. "So we actually provide a way of suggesting how managers who are undertaking these programs can use the data that they usually already have to come up with the best target."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The goal is to determine the ideal range of population where managers can begin to recover the native species or ecosystem function that's been harmed by the invasive species. And often the answer isn't simply linear, he says. "It's not like if you reduce the invasive species a little bit more, you can bring more native species back — there's often a threshold you need to hit for recovery to begin."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;If the number is too low, the invasive species will still damage the ecosystem. If the number is too high, managers might be putting in more work than they need to.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Their research on functional eradication aims to help invasive species specialists more quickly find that crucial number.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/invasive-species-management" data-id="5" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651221690" data-published-at="1616766506" id="rebelltitem5">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"
            data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg4MTMxOC9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY3NzI0MTMwNX0.YW1Gq5AEMTCnJpiG5uba5BQnLA9rGsn1iXeLKPSP5Tw/img.jpg?width=980"
            id="ae5a1"
            width="800"
            height="744"
            data-rm-shortcode-id="c1063e4af17743a2f2d82f523c745246" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p>An invasive red lionfish in the Bahamas. James St. John / CC BY 2.0</p></small></div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-6" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/invasive-species-management" data-id="6" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651221690" data-published-at="1616766506" id="rebelltitem6">&lt;p&gt;For example, they calculate that reducing populations of another deadly invasive species, the red lionfish, to below 25 individuals per hectare in the tropical Western Atlantic "could prevent predation‐induced declines in native fishes and result in low rates of recolonization."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h1&gt;Doing the Work&lt;/h1&gt;&lt;p&gt;Having that data is a critical first step. But getting the work done on the ground is another issue. For managers working to control invasive species in aquatic systems it can be particularly challenging — and resource-intensive.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"With a lot of terrestrial invasions, especially involving things that don't move like plants, it's pretty easy to know when you succeed and when you've gotten them all," says Grosholz. "But when you're thinking about things in the water — in lakes or estuaries or oceans — you often can't even see them. So in most cases, when the horse is out of the barn, it's going to be very difficult to eradicate something in these ecosystems."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;That's where community scientists can come in, he says.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"We have throughout this [work in California] relied on volunteers to help pull the traps and count the crabs. We put out 90 traps a day and pull in thousands of crabs a day," he says. "Volunteers were really instrumental in reaching our goals for the project. And now they're really instrumental in maintaining this low population level."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The key to community science, though, is finding people who are concerned enough to do the work — and have the time.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;When those two things align significant conservation work can be accomplished — and it's work that will become increasingly important as climate change and other environmental pressures further threaten biodiversity.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Invasive species have contributed to many examples of loss of biodiversity, but driving species to extinction isn't the only threat, says Grosholz. Invasive species can also cause "functional extinction" of native species.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"In other words, the role in the ecosystem — whether it's exchanging energy biomass or contributing to trophic support — can be eliminated," he says. "So we may not entirely lose the native species, but we may lose the function they provide to the ecosystem — and that's really important, too."&lt;/p&gt;</div>

                    &lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://therevelator.org/author/taralohan/" target="_blank"&gt;&lt;em&gt;Tara Lohan &lt;/em&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;em&gt;is deputy editor of The Revelator and has worked for more than a decade as a digital editor and environmental journalist focused on the intersections of energy, water and climate. Her work has been published by The Nation, American Prospect, High Country News, Grist, Pacific Standard and others. She is the editor of two books on the global water crisis.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Reposted with permission from &lt;a href="https://therevelator.org/invasive-green-crabs" target="_blank"&gt;The Revelator.&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;<div class="around-the-web"><div class="from-your-site__headline">From Your Site Articles</div>

<h6 class="widget__headline h6">
<a aria-label="Africa’s Elephants Are Two Different Species, and Both Are Endangered" class="widget__headline-text custom-post-headline" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/elephant-species-africa-endangered-2651210823.html">
        Africa’s Elephants Are Two Different Species, and Both Are Endangered
    </a>
</h6>
<div class="social-author clearfix">
<div class="social-author__avatar image">
<div class="cover-all image" style='background-image: url("https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8xNzQxMzM2NS9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY2OTE1NTE2M30.aHAnjzcgPkB6_WqIedJyVdqvxXmBk3A_csOfZcTG7ek/img.jpg?width=210")'></div>

<a class="social-author__name" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/u/oliviarosane">Olivia Rosane</a>
</div>

<span class="social-date__text">25 March</span>
</div>
<a class="widget__section js-load-brick-on-click" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/animals/">Animals</a>
</div><div class="widget__head"><a aria-label="Africa’s Elephants Are Two Different Species, and Both Are Endangered" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/elephant-species-africa-endangered-2651210823.html">

"\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_8_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 8}, true, "new_amp": "\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_9_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>Africa's <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/elephants" target="_self">elephants</a> are in trouble, and human activity is to blame. </p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/elephant-species-africa-endangered" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651210823" data-published-at="1616699758" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;For the first time, the International Union for Conservation of Nature (IUCN) Red List assessed Africa's elephants as two separate species: the African forest elephant (Loxodonta cyclotis) and the African savanna elephant (Loxodonta africana). They found that both species are &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/endangered-species" target="_self"&gt;endangered&lt;/a&gt;, and the forest elephant critically so.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Africa's elephants play key roles in ecosystems, economies and in our collective imagination all over the world," IUCN Red List Director General Dr. Bruno Oberle said in a &lt;a href="https://www.iucn.org/news/species/202103/african-elephant-species-now-endangered-and-critically-endangered-iucn-red-list" target="_blank"&gt;press release&lt;/a&gt;. "Today's new IUCN Red List assessments of both African elephant species underline the persistent pressures faced by these iconic animals."&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/elephant-species-africa-endangered" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651210823" data-published-at="1616699758" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;div id="ddff8" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="2f6e6ed00b7f531e2137cb703194843e"&gt;&lt;blockquote class="twitter-tweet twitter-custom-tweet" data-twitter-tweet-id="1375070336601968640" data-partner="rebelmouse"&gt;&lt;div style="margin:1em 0"&gt;BREAKING NEWS: African elephant species now Endangered and Critically Endangered - IUCN Red List

With today's upda… https://t.co/RXRmB10DBE&lt;/div&gt; &amp;mdash; IUCN Red List (@IUCN Red List)&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/IUCNRedList/statuses/1375070336601968640"&gt;1616677290.0&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;/div&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/elephant-species-africa-endangered" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651210823" data-published-at="1616699758" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;p&gt;The last time that the IUCN assessed Africa's elephant population was in 2008, &lt;a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/25/science/elephants-africa-endangered.html" target="_blank"&gt;The New York Times reported&lt;/a&gt;. At that point, all of Africa's elephants were considered as a single species, and were listed as "vulnerable," one step better than endangered.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;However, mounting genetic evidence indicates that there are two species of elephants on the continent. Africa's forest elephants typically live in West Africa and in tropical rainforests in Central Africa, IUCN pointed out. Savanna elephants prefer open areas like grasslands and deserts. The two species' ranges rarely overlap, and a &lt;a href="https://www.iucn.org/sites/dev/files/content/documents/2019-03-15-final-taxanomy_report-african-elephant-sg.pdf" target="_blank"&gt;2019 study&lt;/a&gt; found that they rarely reproduce with each other.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;There are also physical and life-cycle differences between the two species, according to &lt;a href="https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2021/mar/25/african-elephants-now-red-list-two-species-both-nearer-extinction" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;The Guardian&lt;/a&gt;. Forest elephants are smaller, gestate longer, and have oval ears and smaller tusks. Savanna elephants live in larger family units, have larger ears and their skulls are shaped differently. Some scientists have questioned splitting them into distinct species, because they do sometimes cross breed. However, others say the new categorization is long overdue.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"The separation between them is probably greater than the separation between lions and tigers," Dr. Alfred Roca, a geneticist at the University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign, told The New York Times.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/elephant-species-africa-endangered" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651210823" data-published-at="1616699758" id="rebelltitem4">&lt;p&gt;The new categorization has important &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/conservation" target="_self"&gt;conservation&lt;/a&gt; implications. For one thing, it reveals how much trouble both species, but especially the forest elephants, are really in. The new assessment found that the population of forest elephants had fallen more than 86 percent in the last 31 years, while the population of savanna elephants has decreased by at least 60 percent in the last 50 years, according to the IUCN. As of 2016, there were 415,000 elephants of both species alive in Africa.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For both species, the main drivers of the decline have been &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/poaching" target="_self"&gt;poaching&lt;/a&gt;, which peaked in 2011, and habitat loss through the conversion of their homes for agriculture and other human uses.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"With persistent demand for ivory and escalating human pressures on Africa's wild lands, concern for Africa's elephants is high, and the need to creatively conserve and wisely manage these animals and their habitats is more acute than ever," Dr. Kathleen Gobush, lead assessor of the African elephants and member of the IUCN SSC African Elephant Specialist Group, said in the press release.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/elephant-species-africa-endangered" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651210823" data-published-at="1616699758" id="rebelltitem5">&lt;p&gt;Viewing them as distinct species can help with these conservation efforts, Gobush further explained to The Guardian. So far, savanna elephants have dominated research and the popular imagination, while forest elephants are less studied.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"This reclassification allows dedicated attention to each animal – the forest elephant and the savanna elephant – and then to tailor conservation plans according to each species' needs, which are different," Gobush said.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;One bit of good news from the assessment is that conservation can work when done right. Subpopulations of forest elephants are doing well in the most protected areas of Gabon and the Republic of the Congo, according to the IUCN. The same is true for the largest single grouping of savanna elephants, who live in the Kavango-Zambezi Transfrontier Conservation Area.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;However, the stakes are high. Elephants play an important role in their ecosystems, Gobush told The New York Times. Forest elephants are the sole dispersers of some tree species, while both create new habitats for other animals by eating plants and knocking down trees.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Both of them really could be considered gardeners tending to the vegetation, more than probably any other animal," Gobush said. "We just can't afford to lose them, really."&lt;/p&gt;</div>

<div class="widget tag-chemicals tag-public-health tag-environmental-justice tag-cancer tag-air-pollution tag-pfas post-section--health-stories" data-category="Health + Wellness" elid="2651221968">

        Back-to-Back Hurricanes in Central America Push Migrants North, Adding to Humanitarian Crisis
    </a>

"order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>When back-to-back <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/hurricanes">hurricanes</a> struck Central America last November, families in the region were already facing a food shortage, violence and economic decline from the ongoing COVID-19 pandemic. </p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/central-america-hurricanes-climate-refugees" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651211219" data-published-at="1616695680" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;Four months later, people affected by Hurricanes Eta and Iota are struggling to recover, and the impacts of the storms are just beginning to be felt by agriculture communities, prompting some experts to link climate change to the recent surge in migrants arriving at the US-Mexico border, &lt;a href="https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/2021/3/22/22335816/border-crisis-migrant-hurricane-eta-iota" target="_blank"&gt;Vox reported&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"The hurricanes were... the last in the series of what was a devastating year," Meghan López, the International Rescue Committee's regional vice president for Latin America, &lt;a href="https://www.cnn.com/2021/03/24/us/border-climate-change-covid/index.html" target="_blank"&gt;told CNN&lt;/a&gt;. "To have the pandemic on top of that, to have aid to the region cut, all of these things create this pressure cooker where there's no escape valve... And the only escape valve is to try to flee the terrible situation people are living in... People are making desperate decisions."&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/central-america-hurricanes-climate-refugees" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651211219" data-published-at="1616695680" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;p&gt;The hurricanes left "200 people dead and another 5.3 million people in need of assistance, including more than 1.8 million children," according to UNICEF, Vox reported. They also came at the same time as harvest, causing some regions to lose 40 percent of corn crops and 65 percent of bean crops.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"(Hurricane) Eta – plus the pandemic – left us with nothing," a Honduran father told CNN, after being deported by U.S. authorities to Reynosa, Mexico.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/central-america-hurricanes-climate-refugees" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651211219" data-published-at="1616695680" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;p&gt;When major storms have hit the region in the past, farmers tended to move to urban areas for better employment opportunities, said Kayly Ober, a senior advocate and program manager for the Climate Displacement Program at Refugees International. Yet due to the pandemic, these same opportunities haven't been available, Vox reported.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The pandemic is also limiting opportunities at the border, where an increasing amount of unaccompanied minors are being held beyond legal limits in facilities because the Department of Health and Human Services has run out of space to house people, CNN reported.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/central-america-hurricanes-climate-refugees" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651211219" data-published-at="1616695680" id="rebelltitem5">&lt;p&gt;In the U.S., political leaders are struggling to determine the best approach to solving the border crisis. "Politically, it's never the "right time" for immigration reform," Veronica Escobar, a Democratic representative from El Paso, Texas, wrote in a recent opinion piece &lt;a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/24/opinion/border-migrants-central-america.html" target="_blank"&gt;published in The New York Times&lt;/a&gt;. "The good news is that we now have an administration willing to work on the issue."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;On Wednesday, President Joe Biden announced that Vice President Kamala Harris would lead the way in addressing immigration issues on the southern border. Harris' approach will focus on slowing the flow of migrants by determining "the root causes" of why people are coming north in the first place, &lt;a href="https://www.politico.com/news/2021/03/24/kamala-harris-immigration-border-surge-477810" target="_blank"&gt;POLITICO reported&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/central-america-hurricanes-climate-refugees" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651211219" data-published-at="1616695680" id="rebelltitem4">&lt;p&gt;While running for president, Biden "proposed spending $4 billion over four years to tackle violence, climate change and government corruption in the Northern Triangle region — comprised of El Salvador, Guatemala and Honduras," POLITICO reported. Ober told Vox that the Biden administration is putting too much emphasis on stopping migrants from coming north, rather than viewing it "with a humanitarian lens." &lt;br&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Other experts have criticized the U.S. for its lack of international aid, leaving migrants with no other choice but to come north. "Many families have nothing to go back to and are now left with little options to survive," Laurent Duvillier, a spokesperson for UNICEF's Latin America and Caribbean regional office, told Vox. "Unless more humanitarian support is provided to Central American countries affected by these tropical storms, unless conditions are created in communities for people to be able to stay, it is expected that more families will migrate north in search for a better future for their children."&lt;/p&gt;</div>

"order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>On Saturday, March 27, people around the world will celebrate the annual Earth Hour, albeit in a slightly different way. </p><p>This <a href="https://www.earthhour.org/our-mission" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">annual tradition</a>, first launched by World Wildlife Fund (WWF) and its partners in Sydney in 2007, involves participants from more than 180 countries switching off their lights on the last Saturday in March in order to call attention to the <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change/" target="_self">climate crisis</a> and <a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/biodiversity" target="_self">biodiversity</a> loss. This year, the organizers are <a href="https://www.earthhour.org/new-in-2021" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">adding something extra</a>: <span style="background-color: initial;">a virtual spotlight that can be shined on the Earth by sharing their video.</span></p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/earth-hour-2021" data-id="1" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651208598" data-published-at="1616694971" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"
            data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg3ODAzNy9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYyNzY4MDc4OH0.bbBJ5SZ7UIRH7UIzF_Rs9SQfZItT7ZsZzH0I8zpHuSw/img.png?width=980"
            id="dc61b"
            width="1418"
            height="792"
            data-rm-shortcode-id="3a4fe40b6559dcd2f19ef5bb22323580" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p>The Eiffel Tower in Paris, France, is among the major landmarks that will turn off its lights for Earth Hour on March 27, 2021. Antoine Antoniol / Getty Images</p></small>&lt;p&gt;"Our goal is simple," organizers wrote. "Put the spotlight on our planet and make it the most watched video in the world on March 27 (or beyond!) so that as many people as possible hear our message."&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;The virtual spotlight comes about a year into the &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/tag/coronavirus" target="_self"&gt;coronavirus&lt;/a&gt; pandemic, as many countries remain under some type of safety regulation. While COVID-19 necessitates an online celebration, it also reflects the importance of protecting the natural world.&lt;br&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"Protecting nature is our moral responsibility but losing it also increases our vulnerability to pandemics, accelerates climate change, and threatens our food security," WWF International Director General Marco Lambertini said in a &lt;a href="https://wwf.panda.org/wwf_news/press_releases//?uNewsID=1814966&amp;amp;utm_source=feedburner&amp;amp;utm_medium=feed&amp;amp;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+wwfmedia+%28WWF+-+Media+%26+Resources+for+Journalists%29" target="_blank"&gt;press release&lt;/a&gt;. "We must stop taking nature for granted, respect its intrinsic value, and — importantly — value the crucial services it provides to our health, wellbeing and economy."&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/earth-hour-2021" data-id="2" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651208598" data-published-at="1616694971" id="rebelltitem2"><h3 data-role="headline"> </h3>&lt;div id="5e7e7" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="3b23775f17d06eebdfefa1c7a8c797d1"&gt;&lt;blockquote class="twitter-tweet twitter-custom-tweet" data-twitter-tweet-id="1374936579127435267" data-partner="rebelmouse"&gt;&lt;div style="margin:1em 0"&gt;Tick. Tock. Tick. Tock. 🕣The time has finally come as #EarthHour is in 2 days! 
Here’s how to take part in our Virt… https://t.co/jNddKv6lAK&lt;/div&gt; &amp;mdash; Earth Hour Official (@Earth Hour Official)&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/earthhour/statuses/1374936579127435267"&gt;1616645400.0&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;span style="background-color: initial;"&gt;  &lt;/span&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/earth-hour-2021" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651208598" data-published-at="1616694971" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;p&gt;This year's Earth Hour also comes at a crucial moment in the international push to protect the world's plants and animals. In a few months, world leaders will gather in Kunming, China, for the Conference of the Parties to the Convention on Biological Diversity. Scientists, activists and the UN are hoping the summit will result in an agreement to &lt;a href="https://www.ecowatch.com/un-biodiversity-sixth-mass-extinction-2644807009.html" target="_self"&gt;protect 30 percent of land and oceans by 2030.&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Earth Hour said they hoped their video would build momentum toward this conference. At the same time, UN Secretary-General Antonio Guterres recorded a &lt;a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=V_m-6TsEyf4" target="_blank"&gt;video&lt;/a&gt; in support of Earth Hour.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;"In this make or break year, let your actions and voices send a clear message to leaders everywhere," Guterres said. "Now is the time to be bold and ambitious. Let's show the world that we are determined to protect the one home we all share."&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/earth-hour-2021" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651208598" data-published-at="1616694971" id="rebelltitem4"><h3 data-role="headline"> </h3>&lt;span style="display:block;position:relative;padding-top:56.25%;" class="rm-shortcode" data-rm-shortcode-id="9c7ddd5196be21f61ca0130fde9fa9c4"&gt;&lt;iframe lazy-loadable="true" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/V_m-6TsEyf4?rel=0" width="100%" height="auto"  frameborder="0" scrolling="no" style="position:absolute;top:0;left:0;width:100%;height:100%;"&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt;&lt;/span&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/earth-hour-2021" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651208598" data-published-at="1616694971" id="rebelltitem5">&lt;p&gt;&lt;br&gt;This year's Earth Hour will also include the traditional lights-out celebration. Major landmarks, including the Eiffel Tower, Tokyo Skytree, Hong Kong's Victoria Harbor, Brandenburg Gate in Berlin, the Colosseum in Rome, Sydney Opera House and Gardens by the Bay in Singapore, will all go dark. Anyone can join by simply turning off lights for an hour beginning at 8:30 p.m. local time.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To participate online, keep an eye on Earth Hour's pages on &lt;a href="https://www.instagram.com/earthhourofficial/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Instagram&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/earthhour/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Facebook&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="https://twitter.com/earthhour" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Twitter&lt;/a&gt; and share the video when it drops. It can be added to a social media story, reposted or even sent in private messages.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;'We urgently need to take action to prevent further degradation of our natural world, for securing our own future," John Kani, an actor and environmentalist who will lend his voice to the video, said in the press release. "Join me this Earth Hour when we collectively raise our voice for nature to secure a greener, healthier future for all."&lt;/p&gt;</div>

<h6 class="widget__headline h6">
<a aria-label="Why Companies’ Net-Zero Emissions Pledges Should Trigger Skepticism" class="widget__headline-text custom-post-headline" data-type="text" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/net-zero-companies-2651210059.html">
        Why Companies’ Net-Zero Emissions Pledges Should Trigger Skepticism
    </a>
</h6>
<div class="social-author clearfix">
<div class="social-author__avatar image">
<div class="cover-all image" style='background-image: url("https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy82NzI1NTU3L29yaWdpbi5qcGciLCJleHBpcmVzX2F0IjoxNjQ3NTIxOTEwfQ.RRiCDsOja8F3DatceLE6FbT3uo6F9-1QV9_s0V8Hr34/img.jpg?width=210")'></div>

</div>
<a class="widget__section js-load-brick-on-click" href="https://www.ecowatch.com/climate-change/">Climate</a>

"order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>
	By Oliver Miltenberger and Matthew D. Potts
</p><p>
<a href="https://sciencebasedtargets.org/companies-taking-action" target="_blank">Hundreds of companies</a>, including major emitters like <a href="https://www.united.com/ual/en/us/fly/company/global-citizenship/environment/100-percent-green.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">United Airlines</a>, <a href="https://www.bp.com/en/global/corporate/news-and-insights/press-releases/bernard-looney-announces-new-ambition-for-bp.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">BP</a> and <a href="https://www.shell.com/media/news-and-media-releases/2021/shell-accelerates-drive-for-net-zero-emissions-with-customer-first-strategy.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Shell</a>, have pledged to reduce their impact on climate change and reach net-zero carbon emissions by 2050. These plans sound ambitious, but what does it actually take to reach net-zero and, more importantly, will it be enough to slow climate change?
</p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
                    &lt;p&gt;
	&lt;br/&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;
                    
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/net-zero-companies" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651210059" data-published-at="1616691195" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;As &lt;a href="https://vcresearch.berkeley.edu/faculty/matthew-potts" target="_blank"&gt;environmental policy&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="https://www.climatecollege.unimelb.edu.au/profiles/oliver-miltenberger" target="_blank"&gt;economics researchers&lt;/a&gt;, we study how companies make these net-zero pledges. Though the pledges make great press releases, net-zero is more complicated and potentially problematic than it may seem.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;What Is 'Net-Zero' Emissions?&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;The gold standard for reaching net-zero emissions &lt;a href="https://ghgprotocol.org/corporate-standard" target="_blank"&gt;looks like this&lt;/a&gt;: A company identifies and reports all emissions it is responsible for creating, it reduces them as much as possible, and then – if it still has emissions it cannot reduce – it invests in projects that either prevent emissions elsewhere or pull carbon out of the air to reach a "net-zero" balance on paper.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The process &lt;a href="https://www.carbontrust.com/news-and-events/insights/net-zero-an-ambition-in-need-of-a-definition" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;is complex and still largely unregulated and ill-defined&lt;/a&gt;. As a result, companies have a lot of discretion over how they report their emissions. For example, &lt;a href="https://www.riotinto.com/en/sustainability/climate-change" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;a multinational mining company&lt;/a&gt; might count emissions from extracting and processing ore but not the emissions produced by transporting it.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Companies also have discretion over how much they rely on what are known as offsets – the projects they can fund to reduce emissions. The &lt;a href="https://www.shell.com/promos/business-customers-promos/download-latest-scenario-sky/_jcr_content.stream/1530643931055/eca19f7fc0d20adbe830d3b0b27bcc9ef72198f5/shell-scenario-sky.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;oil giant Shell&lt;/a&gt;, for example, projects that it will both achieve net-zero emissions by 2050 and continue to produce high levels of fossil fuel through that year and beyond. How? It proposes to offset the bulk of its fossil-fuel-related emissions through massive nature-based projects that capture and store carbon, such as forest and ocean restoration. In fact, Shell alone plans to &lt;a href="https://www.reuters.com/article/us-shell-carbon-offsets-graphic-idUSKBN2AC1CR" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;deploy more of these offsets by 2030&lt;/a&gt; than were available globally in 2019.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Environmentalists may welcome Shell's newfound conservationist agenda, but what if other oil companies, the airline industries, the shipping sectors and the U.S. government all propose a similar solution? Is there enough land and ocean realistically available for offsets, and is simply restoring environments without fundamentally changing the business-as-usual paradigm really a solution to climate change?&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/net-zero-companies" data-id="2" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651210059" data-published-at="1616691195" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"
            data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg3NzEyOC9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYyNDgxMDc2M30.tWfpcEfCGKH5mlqQ1mBBjh6nUYczD7FMEX-cruWZ_K0/img.png?width=980"
            id="2bf96"
            width="1226"
            height="870"
            data-rm-shortcode-id="d12ed0cb56e72630985467913b2c4018" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   /&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/net-zero-companies" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651210059" data-published-at="1616691195" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;h2&gt;Concerns About Voluntary Carbon Markets&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;Outside of &lt;a href="https://www.epa.gov/emissions-trading-resources/what-emissions-trading" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;compliance emissions markets&lt;/a&gt;, which primarily focus on government regulation in the &lt;a href="https://ec.europa.eu/clima/policies/ets_en" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;energy sector&lt;/a&gt;, voluntary markets create most of the offsets that are used to reach net-zero.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Voluntary markets are organized and operated by a diverse range of groups where anyone can participate. Have you ever seen the option to offset your flight? That offset probably happens through a voluntary carbon market. The activities that produce the offsets include projects like &lt;a href="https://climatetrust.org/forest-carbon-projects-faq/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;forestry&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="https://www.thebluecarboninitiative.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;ocean management&lt;/a&gt;, waste management, agricultural practices, fuel switching and renewable energy. As the name implies, they are voluntary and therefore largely unregulated.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Because of the wave of net-zero pledges and subsequent demand for offsets, voluntary carbon markets are under pressure to expand quickly. &lt;a href="https://www.iif.com/tsvcm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;A task force&lt;/a&gt; launched by United Nations Special Envoy on Climate Action Mark Carney and involving several major companies released a &lt;a href="https://www.iif.com/tsvcm/Main-Page/Publications/ID/4254/Taskforce-Establishes-Core-Carbon-Principles-Publishes-Roadmap-for-Scaling-Voluntary-Carbon-Markets" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;sweeping blueprint&lt;/a&gt; at Davos 2021 that predicts voluntary carbon markets need to grow fifteenfold over the next decade. It suggests that the net-zero surge represents one of the largest commercial opportunities of our time – prompting keen interest from &lt;a href="https://www.blackrock.com/corporate/investor-relations/blackrock-client-letter" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;investors&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="https://www.uschamber.com/series/above-the-fold/update-the-chambers-approach-climate" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;big business&lt;/a&gt;. It also identifies and proposes solutions to some persistent challenges and critiques of voluntary carbon offset markets.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/net-zero-companies" data-id="4" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651210059" data-published-at="1616691195" id="rebelltitem4">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"
            data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg3NzE1My9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYzMDk2ODkyNX0.hJbBDsIx_c5lxWMdbQzhMBtfnQuFEH4uz2V0tq1fNR0/img.png?width=980"
            id="a9e3a"
            width="1238"
            height="714"
            data-rm-shortcode-id="656cc3536e3758224bc5bca07a886597" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   /&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/net-zero-companies" data-id="5" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651210059" data-published-at="1616691195" id="rebelltitem5">&lt;p&gt;Some critics of the blueprint argue that it &lt;a href="https://carbonplan-assets.s3.amazonaws.com/docs/Offset-Task-Force-Comment-Letter-01-05-2021.pdf" target="_blank"&gt;overlooks deeper problems&lt;/a&gt; rooted in the overall reliance on and effectiveness of voluntary carbon markets as a solution.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Though there is historical &lt;a href="https://features.propublica.org/brazil-carbon-offsets/inconvenient-truth-carbon-credits-dont-work-deforestation-redd-acre-cambodia/" target="_blank"&gt;evidence of misuse&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href="https://greenfinanceobservatory.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/Scaling-up-GFO-analysis-final4.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;plenty of criticism&lt;/a&gt;, voluntary carbon markets are not inherently bad or useless in the pursuit of climate targets. In fact, quite the opposite. Some voluntary carbon market projects, in addition to &lt;a href="https://www.edf.org/media/carbon-offsets-when-done-right-can-reduce-emissions-and-support-paris-agreement-edf-and-engie" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;mitigating climate change&lt;/a&gt;, provide &lt;a href="https://doi.org/10.1080/14693062.2020.1724070" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;other benefits&lt;/a&gt;, such as improvements to biodiversity habitats, water quality, soil health and socioeconomic opportunities.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;However, there are real concerns about the ability of voluntary markets to legitimately deliver what they promise. Common concerns include &lt;a href="https://news.berkeley.edu/2019/05/07/new-paper-states-cap-and-trade-program-is-falling-short-of-goals/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;questions about the permanence of the projects&lt;/a&gt; for storing carbon long term, verifying that offsets actually reduce emissions beyond a business-as-usual scenario and confirming that credits are not being used more than once. These and other challenges expose voluntary carbon markets to potential manipulation, greenwashing, unintended consequences and, regrettably, failure to achieve their purpose.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="http://voluntarycarbonmarket.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;It's getting better&lt;/a&gt;, but over-reliance on this method for counterbalancing emissions does risk some entities' using offsets as a &lt;a href="https://www.nrdc.org/stories/should-you-buy-carbon-offsets" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;right to pollute&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-6" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/net-zero-companies" data-id="6" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651210059" data-published-at="1616691195" id="rebelltitem6">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"
            data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg3NzE1Ny9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY0MzU5MzI1MH0.QSJZpRF75WGe_2Ogd6ubqWA_6bn0LpTl2yGzN39dt08/img.png?width=980"
            id="d2a9c"
            width="1260"
            height="1268"
            data-rm-shortcode-id="7a9bc368163ac21757a3e395c7aa6bfc" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   /&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-7" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/net-zero-companies" data-id="7" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651210059" data-published-at="1616691195" id="rebelltitem7">&lt;h2&gt;Can Global Ecology Meet the Demand?&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;Voluntary carbon markets can improve landscapes and help make up for unavoidable emissions. However, they cannot accommodate all of the developed world's net-zero targets.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Most of these initiatives have not yet started, yet emitters from developed countries are already seeking offsets outside their borders. This is raising concerns that wealthier companies may be placing the burden of their emissions onto poorer countries that can produce offsets cheaply, begging the notion of a newfound climate colonialism. Local communities may benefit from some environmental improvements or socioeconomic opportunities, but should economically developed polluters be forcing that decision?&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Beyond ethics, in statistical terms, there is simply not enough ecological capacity to offset the world's emissions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Take the interest in using forests as offset solutions. There are around &lt;a href="http://dx.doi.org/10.1038/nature14967" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;3 trillion trees&lt;/a&gt; on Earth today with room for about &lt;a href="http://doi.org/10.1126/science.aax0848" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;1 to 2.5 trillion more&lt;/a&gt;. The &lt;a href="https://trilliontreesinitiative.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Trillion Tree Initiative&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="https://www.1t.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;1T program&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href="https://trilliontrees.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Trillion Trees&lt;/a&gt;, and the CEO of &lt;a href="https://www.independent.co.uk/climate-change/news/reddit-yishan-wong-trees-b1803102.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;Reddit&lt;/a&gt;, among others, aim to plant a trillion trees each. From just a few examples, there is already a paradoxical impasse.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Offsets can realistically do only so much for reaching climate targets. That is why the focus must turn toward reducing rather than offsetting global emissions. Voluntary carbon markets serve a critical role as innovation sandboxes for creative offset solutions, and they are mobilizing the private sector to act; however, they must be limited.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;While some prominent organizations are pursuing net-zero, most &lt;a href="https://climateactiontracker.org/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;businesses and governments&lt;/a&gt; have not yet pledged, let alone developed, clear and plausible road maps to meet targets in line with a 2050 net-zero global economy.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-8" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/net-zero-companies" data-id="8" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651210059" data-published-at="1616691195" id="rebelltitem8">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"
            data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg3NzE2My9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYxNzE1MzkzOX0.9VuP1Mdh1eiL5K7ATQQqwMssfo7ojVGBPAYUmxebI78/img.png?width=980"
            id="28e62"
            width="1322"
            height="880"
            data-rm-shortcode-id="a955880f1c1a4912de8d507183ca43e0" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   /&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-9" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/net-zero-companies" data-id="9" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651210059" data-published-at="1616691195" id="rebelltitem9">&lt;h2&gt;The Needed Goal: A Negative Net&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href="https://www.ipcc.ch/site/assets/uploads/sites/2/2019/06/SR15_Full_Report_Low_Res.pdf" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;The Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change suggests&lt;/a&gt; that the world can keep global warming in check if emissions are cut in half by 2030, compared to 2010 levels, and reach net-zero by midcentury. However, it also states a need for greenhouse gas removal beyond net-zero emissions targets.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The real act of climate cleanup begins at net-negative emissions for all greenhouse gases. Only then will their atmospheric concentrations finally begin shrinking. That feat will require more renewable energy, widespread infrastructure and transportation developments, improved land management and investments in carbon capturing activities and technologies.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;While net-zero is a critical step toward addressing climate change, it must be achieved smartly. And, importantly, it can't be the end goal.&lt;/p&gt;</div>

                    &lt;p&gt;
	&lt;em&gt;&lt;a href="https://theconversation.com/profiles/oliver-miltenberger-797703" target="_blank"&gt;Oliver Miltenberger&lt;/a&gt; is a &lt;/em&gt;&lt;em&gt;Ph.D. Candidate in Environmental Economics, The University of Melbourne.&lt;/em&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;
	&lt;em&gt;&lt;a href="https://theconversation.com/profiles/matthew-d-potts-1215756" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank"&gt;Matthew D. Potts&lt;/a&gt; is a &lt;/em&gt;&lt;em&gt;Professor, S.J. Hall Chair in Forest Economics, University of California, Berkeley.&lt;/em&gt;
&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;
	&lt;em&gt;Disclosure statement: &lt;/em&gt;&lt;em&gt;Matthew Potts is also a scientific advisor for Carbon Direct. &lt;/em&gt;&lt;em&gt;&lt;em&gt;Oliver Miltenberger does not work for, consult, own shares in or receive funding from any company or organization that would benefit from this article, and has disclosed no relevant affiliations beyond their academic appointment.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/em&gt;

"\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_8_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 8}, {"amp": "\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_9_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003camp-ad width=336 height=280\n    type=\"doubleclick\"\n    data-slot=\"/5376056/ecowatch_content_9_amp\"\n    data-multi-size=\"320x50,300x250\"\u003e\n\u003c/amp-ad\u003e", "order": 9}, {"amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "display": true, "new_amp": "\u003cdiv class=\"placeholder-last-ad\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e", "order": 10}], "adsOrder": [2]}
        </script><div class="body-description"><div class="widget__brief"><p>By Noah Horowitz </p><p>While the energy efficiency of America's smart televisions has improved greatly since flat panel models were first introduced, some of the energy savings are at risk due to new "smart wake" features that can waste a lot of power when the TV is in standby mode.</p></div>
<div class="content-container"></div>
<div class="js-appear-on-expand"><template>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-1" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/smart-tv-energy-efficiency" data-id="1" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651208824" data-published-at="1616691182" id="rebelltitem1">&lt;p&gt;These features provide the user with the convenience of waking their TV through a voice command to a nearby smart speaker, or to seamlessly shift from watching content on a tablet or phone to the TV, without using a remote control. Our extensive laboratory testing on the standby power of 10 different models found that in many cases, enabling these features caused a TV's overall annual electricity consumption to skyrocket by as much as 75 percent.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-2" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/smart-tv-energy-efficiency" data-id="2" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651208824" data-published-at="1616691182" id="rebelltitem2">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"
            data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg3NjgzMS9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYyODk0MDIzOH0.ukxNN39aeuNYF-NfYQ2nen58cpayS00FLt3OUpMwS_E/img.jpg?width=980"
            id="93997"
            width="1272"
            height="962"
            data-rm-shortcode-id="536434af3db5d45c0bcaaf3b53589f9b" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   /&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-3" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/smart-tv-energy-efficiency" data-id="3" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651208824" data-published-at="1616691182" id="rebelltitem3">&lt;p&gt;All that extra standby power adds up. NRDC estimates it will cost purchasers of 2021 TVs who enable smart wake features an additional $750 million on their utility bills over these TVs' seven-year lifetime, barring future manufacturer design improvements. The extra electricity consumption also will lead to more than 3 million tons of additional carbon dioxide emissions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Spoiler alert, Samsung and LG TVs have found a way to support smart wake on their internet-connected televisions WITHOUT a noticeable increase in standby power levels. Other models we tested, however, were like vampires continuously guzzling electricity while waiting to be fully awakened.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-4" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/smart-tv-energy-efficiency" data-id="4" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651208824" data-published-at="1616691182" id="rebelltitem4">&lt;h3&gt;What Are 'Smart Wake' Features?&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;The vast majority of new TVs offer the user the ability to be connected wirelessly to a smart speaker like the Amazon Echo (which many simply call Alexa). The user can then wake or control the TV simply with voice commands by saying things like, "Alexa turn on the TV" or "OK Google, turn on the Knicks game." Another option is "wake by cast," which allows a user who is viewing a movie or show on a tablet or phone to click on the little casting icon, and their TV will quickly wake and display the same content. Lastly, users can download an app to turn their phone into a virtual remote control that can wake and control their TV. These three features are forms of "smart wake" that avoid the hassle of having to locate and use a remote control.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-5" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/smart-tv-energy-efficiency" data-id="5" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651208824" data-published-at="1616691182" id="rebelltitem5">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"
            data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg3Njg2OS9vcmlnaW4uanBnIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY3MjAyMDc3MX0.j9BQR0JHhl5tR0xE-IP5Pujo_K72u2CjWV1Tnzsn2Fk/img.jpg?width=980"
            id="a9d2f"
            width="1272"
            height="848"
            data-rm-shortcode-id="0c34a789dc377175b11d908000759939" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p><em></em><em>iStock / Diy13</em></p></small></div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-6" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/smart-tv-energy-efficiency" data-id="6" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651208824" data-published-at="1616691182" id="rebelltitem6">&lt;h3&gt;How Did We Test the TVs?&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;NRDC partnered with Pacific Crest Laboratories (PCL) for the first in-depth study of the standby power of different TVs when these features were enabled. Most of the ten TVs we tested required the user to go into the menu and turn on/enable the smart wake features. Each manufacturer had its own terminology for the settings and in some cases, the user needed to select the Quick Start feature for things to operate properly. We tested a range of TV brands, both major and small, as well as a variety of operating systems (e.g., Roku, Android TV, Amazon Fire TV, etc.) that these TVs are controlled by.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Prior to testing we connected the TV to a live internet signal and downloaded the latest software update. After displaying video content, we turned off the TV and measured its standby power. We then configured the TV so the smart wake features were enabled, including selecting wake on cast and linking the smart speaker to the TV via a wireless connection.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Subsequently, we confirmed whether the smart wake features worked and measured the TV's standby power for 40 minutes. Given that TVs may not fully power down for several minutes, we waited 20 minutes before starting our measurements and then recorded the average standby power over the next 20 minutes.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-7" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/smart-tv-energy-efficiency" data-id="7" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651208824" data-published-at="1616691182" id="rebelltitem7">&lt;h3&gt;What Impact Did Smart Wake Have on TV Standby Power?&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;The average standby power level of TVs tested without any smart wake features enabled was 0.6 watts. Once we turned on the smart wake features, standby power levels jumped dramatically. This table shows the brands tested, along with their operating system (OS). Some of the operating systems like Android TV are used by multiple manufacturers, whereas LG and Samsung have their own proprietary operating systems, WebOS and Tizen, respectively.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-8" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/smart-tv-energy-efficiency" data-id="8" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651208824" data-published-at="1616691182" id="rebelltitem8">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"
            data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg3Njg4NC9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTY2NDE4NjYyOH0.r3tA6yLer3CvzON_4AGHr-iGq-3LNJ4aka8msrU5gss/img.png?width=980"
            id="5e232"
            width="1272"
            height="554"
            data-rm-shortcode-id="d864c6413b21116d35fca8d7fa3739b8" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   /&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-9" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/smart-tv-energy-efficiency" data-id="9" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651208824" data-published-at="1616691182" id="rebelltitem9">&lt;p&gt;Two things to note: a) Samsung and LG TVs supported smart wake features without a noticeable increase in standby power; and b) for all the other TVs tested we saw standby power levels from roughly 5 to 20 watts. We conferred with the &lt;a href="https://neea.org/news/transforming-the-televisions-market" target="_blank"&gt;Northwest Energy Efficiency Alliance&lt;/a&gt; (NEEA), which has tested roughly 40 TVs in both on and standby modes and done lots of great work in this space, and reported an average standby power level of 12.5 watts for models that showed elevated standby power levels with smart wake. (We used this value in our modeling discussed below.)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In follow-up conversations with Vizio, we learned that their TVs support wake by phone (using the phone as a remote control) when their TV is in the default Eco Mode setting and were able to achieve standby power level of less than 1 watt. The 14.4-watt level in the table was based on testing with the Vizio TV's Quick Start setting selected as that was required to get their wake by cast and wake by voice features to work properly.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-10" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/smart-tv-energy-efficiency" data-id="10" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651208824" data-published-at="1616691182" id="rebelltitem10">&lt;h3&gt;National Impacts&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;NRDC and PCL developed a model to quantify the national impact of smart wake features. We excluded Samsung and LG TVs, which together represent just under half of U.S. market share, as they did not show elevated smart wake standby levels. We assumed an incremental standby power level of 11.9 watts, and that half of all users would configure their TVs to use one or more of the smart wake features. (Note: this &lt;a href="https://www.businesswire.com/news/home/20200127005430/en/52-of-Smart-Speaker-Owners-Are-Controlling-TV-With-Voice-Strategy-Analytics#:~:text=BOSTON%2D%2D(BUSINESS%20WIRE)%2D%2D,TV%20device%20at%20least%20weekly" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;article&lt;/a&gt; shows half of smart speaker owners connect them to TVs. While we don't know exactly what percentage use wake by cast or wake by phone, we believe it's significant and likely to grow as the manufacturers make these features easier to use and consumers become more aware of them.)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;On a per TV basis, we assumed an average TV draws around 60 watts of electricity in active use and 0.6 watts in standby. Assuming a duty cycle of 5 hours on and 19 hours off per day, this translates to an annual energy use of 108 kilowatt-hours (kWh) per year. If that same TV had smart wake enabled and drew 12.5 watts in standby, its annual energy use jumped to 191 kWh/yr. — an increase of 76.3 percent. Over the TV's typical 7-year lifetime, it will consume an extra $75 of electricity, and twice that in areas with higher utility rates, like California and Hawaii.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We then quantified the national impacts by assuming that half of the 40 million TVs sold in the U.S. each year have inefficient smart wake designs, and half of those have smart wake enabled. The incremental energy used by these 10 million TVs over their lifetime adds up to:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;5,777-gigawatt hours (GWh) of additional electricity use, which is equivalent to the annual output of two large (500 megawatt) coal-burning power plants&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;$750 million in higher consumer utility bills&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Over 3 million tons of CO2 emissions&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;To put all this extra energy use into perspective, it's roughly equivalent to one year's worth of electricity consumption by all the households in Portland, OR and Tampa combined!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;All of these impacts are just for the U.S. market and become a lot larger when international sales are considered.&lt;/p&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-11" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/smart-tv-energy-efficiency" data-id="11" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651208824" data-published-at="1616691182" id="rebelltitem11">&lt;h3&gt;Where to From Here?&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;p&gt;The good news from this study is that two TV manufacturers already demonstrated that a TV can support all these smart wake features with no energy or performance penalty. We hope our study serves as a call to action for other manufacturers to work with their operating system vendors to provide a good user experience with these smart wake features enabled while achieving similar low standby power levels.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Our policy level recommendations include:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;The test method used by manufacturers and regulators to measure the energy use of TVs must be updated to ensure the TV is connected to the internet during testing and with smart wake features enabled, and that the increased standby power use this may cause is captured and reported.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;The Environmental Protection Agency should update its test method and eligibility criteria for ENERGY STAR® to ensure TVs that qualify for the label have low standby power levels, including when smart wake features are enabled.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;The Federal Trade Commission should update &lt;a href="https://www.ftc.gov/news-events/press-releases/2010/10/starting-2011-ftc-will-require-energyguide-labels-televisions" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"&gt;the testing and reporting instructions&lt;/a&gt; for its yellow ENERGY GUIDE label, which compares the energy use and operating costs of similar sized TVs.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;</div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-13" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/smart-tv-energy-efficiency" data-id="13" data-is-image="True" data-post-id="2651208824" data-published-at="1616691182" id="rebelltitem13">&lt;img
            class="rm-lazyloadable-image rm-shortcode" lazy-loadable="true"
            data-runner-src="https://assets.rebelmouse.io/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJpbWFnZSI6Imh0dHBzOi8vYXNzZXRzLnJibC5tcy8yNTg3NjkyMS9vcmlnaW4ucG5nIiwiZXhwaXJlc19hdCI6MTYxNjk4NjY5Mn0.D0I4m0N5QO2NfgY9GFtXCexKULmOX4o9LVZepED2fM8/img.png?width=980"
            id="10d8b"
            width="1272"
            height="302"
            data-rm-shortcode-id="3a69b436e46fa43da533fee21dcc0784" data-rm-shortcode-name="rebelmouse-image"   /&gt;<small class="image-media media-photo-credit"><p><em></em><em>Courtesy of EPA</em></p></small></div>
<div class="rebellt-item is--desktop col1" data-basename="particle-14" data-href="https://www.ecowatch.com/smart-tv-energy-efficiency" data-id="14" data-is-image="False" data-post-id="2651208824" data-published-at="1616691182" id="rebelltitem14">&lt;p&gt;As a result of our research and conversations with some of the manufacturers and companies that develop the operating systems, we believe these entities now understand this issue and appear committed to trying to make the necessary changes.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Let's hope that in the not too distant future the other TV manufacturers make the necessary software fixes so they catch up to Samsung and LG and we can prevent this unnecessary energy waste and the pollution that comes with it. That's something worth tuning into!&lt;/p&gt;</div>

                    &lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Noah Horowitz is the director of the Center for Energy Efficiency Standards, Climate &amp; Clean Energy Program at Natural Resources Defense Council.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Reposted with permission from &lt;a href="https://www.nrdc.org/experts/noah-horowitz/your-smart-tv-may-have-insomnia-and-guzzle-power-when" target="_blank"&gt;NRDC&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;<div class="around-the-web"><div class="from-your-site__headline">From Your Site Articles</div>
